The Meaning of Istiwa': Domination, Not Settlement
Nasafi refutes the Karramiyyah claim of physical settlement on the Throne using linguistic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karramiyyah interpretation of istiwa' is rejected and how linguistic evidence supports the interpretation of domination.

Core Idea
Istiwa' means domination, not physical settlement.

The Karramiyyah sect wrongly claimed that Allah physically settled on the Throne. Nasafi refutes this by citing exegetes who interpret istiwa' as istila' (domination), supported by a Persian translation and a line of poetry.

Guided Path
1
Read the Karramiyyah claim
Read the first sentence of the passage to understand the claim that Allah settled on the Throne and their proof from the Quran.
Notice that they interpret istiwa' literally.
2
Identify the refutation
Read the next part where Nasafi responds by citing exegetes who say istiwa' means domination (istila'), and note the Persian translation.
The Persian phrase means 'The King is dominant over His Throne'.
3
Examine the poetic evidence
Read the line of poetry and understand how it demonstrates that istiwa' can mean domination in Arabic usage.
The poet says 'Bishr has istawa over Iraq' meaning he dominated it without war.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان معنى الاستواء على العرش ]
قالت الكرَّامية : إن الله تعالى استقرَّ على العرش حتى امتلأ منه حجتهم قوله تعالى: ﴿الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه: ٥].
قلنا لهم: قال بعض أهل التفسير : يعني استولى قيل : بالفارسية: بر عرش پادشاه است (١) وهي جملة فارسية معناها : الملك مستول على عرشه.
يدل عليه قول القائل:
قد استوى بشر على العِرَاقِ من غير سيف ودم مِهْرَاقِ
يعني: استولى.
قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله في قوله: «فعلِمَ أنه قد فعلت الرواية بالمعنى في الحديث ما فعلت» فمن المعلوم والمقرر أن جُلَّ السنة نقل بالمعنى، ومن هذا الباب حديث الجارية المشهور، فقد ورد في أحد طرقه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سألها «أين الله ؟ فأشارت إلى السماء؟» فهذا مما فعلت فيه الرواية بالمعنى ما فعلت أيضًا، لأن الرواية الأخرى لم يرد بها هذا السؤال الذي لم يرد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أي حديث آخر، حيث كان لا يقبل إسلام من يُسلم دون مثل هذه الأسئلة التي لا تتفق مع ما يليق بالله عزّ وجل، فالله تعالى لا أين له حتى يُسأل عنه بالأين ، فهو خالق المكان والزمان وهو على ما عليه كان لم يتغير ولم يتبدل سبحانه وتعالى عما يصفون، وقد غابت هذه القاعدة عن أذهان كثيرن ممن تورّطوا في التشبيه. والله أعلى وأعلم.
Chapter on explaining the meaning of istiwa' over the Throne.
The Karramiyyah said: Allah settled on the Throne until He filled it; their proof is His saying: 'The Most Merciful istawa over the Throne' [Taha:5].
We said to them: Some of the exegetes said: It means He dominated. It is said in Persian: 'Bar 'arsh padshah ast' (١) and it is a Persian sentence meaning: The King is dominant over His Throne.
This is supported by the saying of the poet:
'Bishr has istawa over Iraq without sword and bloodshed'
meaning: He dominated.
I say: The Shaykh, may Allah have mercy on him, was correct in his saying: 'So it is known that transmission by meaning has done its work in the hadith.' It is well established that most of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning. Among this is the famous hadith of the slave girl, for in one of its chains the Prophet, peace be upon him, asked her: 'Where is Allah?' and she pointed to the sky. This too is an instance where transmission by meaning did its work, because the other narration does not contain this question, which has not been reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, in any other hadith. He would not accept someone's Islam without such questions that are inconsistent with what befits Allah, Mighty and Majestic. Allah does not have a 'where' such that He should be asked about it. He is the Creator of place and time, and He is as He ever was, unchanged and unaltered, exalted above what they describe. Many of those who fell into anthropomorphism have overlooked this principle. And Allah is Most High and Most Knowing.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Karramiyyah sect's literal interpretation of istiwa'. The author first states their claim that Allah physically settled on the Throne, citing the Quranic verse. The refutation begins by citing exegetes who interpret istiwa' as istila' (domination), supported by a Persian translation and a poetic line. The editor (likely the same as in Lesson 2) then reinforces the point by linking this to the principle of transmission by meaning, using the hadith of the slave girl as an example. The question 'Where is Allah?' in some narrations is argued to be a transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's actual words, because attributing a location to Allah is impermissible. The author concludes that many who fell into anthropomorphism neglected this principle.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الاستيلاء
العرش
الكرَّامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Istiwa' means physical sitting or settlement.
Correction: Istiwa' in this context means domination (istila'), as supported by exegesis and poetry.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the Karramiyyah claim about istiwa'?
A) By citing a hadith that denies it.
B) By offering linguistic and poetic evidence that istiwa' means domination.
C) By saying the verse is abrogated.
D) By claiming the Quran is unclear.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic istiwa' is interpreted by scholars as Allah's absolute dominion over the Throne, not physical settlement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah being 'above' His creation, do you unconsciously picture a physical location? How does this lesson challenge you to purify your conception of Allah from any resemblance to created things?
?
The poet used the same word (istawa) for a human ruler. Do you ever describe Allah using language that could lower His majesty? What will you do to ensure your speech about Allah is free from anthropomorphism?
?
If someone insisted that the Quranic 'istiwa' implies Allah sitting on a throne, would you be equipped to respond with linguistic evidence? What step will you take to deepen your understanding of the divine attributes so you can defend tawhid?

Transmission by Meaning and the Hadith of the Slave Girl
Nasafi uses the hadith of the slave girl to illustrate how transmission by meaning can introduce problematic wording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of transmission by meaning and how it applies to the hadith about the slave girl, preserving Allah's transcendence beyond place.

Core Idea
Hadith transmitted by meaning may include wording that misrepresents Allah's attributes.

The editor expands on the principle that much of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning. He uses the famous hadith of the slave girl to show that the question 'Where is Allah?' is a result of transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's actual words, because Allah is beyond location.

Guided Path
1
Read the editor's statement
Read the part starting with 'قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله' and note the principle of transmission by meaning.
The editor affirms that most of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning.
2
Analyze the slave girl hadith example
Read how the hadith of the slave girl is presented as an instance of transmission by meaning, focusing on the question 'Where is Allah?'.
This question is not found in other narrations.
3
Understand the theological conclusion
Reflect on why asking 'Where is Allah?' is inappropriate and how this maintains Allah's transcendence.
Allah is the Creator of place and time, so He is not confined to any location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان معنى الاستواء على العرش ]
قالت الكرَّامية : إن الله تعالى استقرَّ على العرش حتى امتلأ منه حجتهم قوله تعالى: ﴿الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه: ٥].
قلنا لهم: قال بعض أهل التفسير : يعني استولى قيل : بالفارسية: بر عرش پادشاه است (١) وهي جملة فارسية معناها : الملك مستول على عرشه.
يدل عليه قول القائل:

يعني: استولى.
قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله في قوله: «فعلِمَ أنه قد فعلت الرواية بالمعنى في الحديث ما فعلت» فمن المعلوم والمقرر أن جُلَّ السنة نقل بالمعنى، ومن هذا الباب حديث الجارية المشهور، فقد ورد في أحد طرقه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سألها «أين الله ؟ فأشارت إلى السماء؟» فهذا مما فعلت فيه الرواية بالمعنى ما فعلت أيضًا، لأن الرواية الأخرى لم يرد بها هذا السؤال الذي لم يرد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أي حديث آخر، حيث كان لا يقبل إسلام من يُسلم دون مثل هذه الأسئلة التي لا تتفق مع ما يليق بالله عزّ وجل، فالله تعالى لا أين له حتى يُسأل عنه بالأين ، فهو خالق المكان والزمان وهو على ما عليه كان لم يتغير ولم يتبدل سبحانه وتعالى عما يصفون، وقد غابت هذه القاعدة عن أذهان كثيرن ممن تورّطوا في التشبيه. والله أعلى وأعلم.

The Karramiyyah said: Allah settled on the Throne until He filled it; their proof is His saying: 'The Most Merciful istawa over the Throne' [Taha:5].
We said to them: Some of the exegetes said: It means He dominated. It is said in Persian: 'Bar 'arsh padshah ast' (١) and it is a Persian sentence meaning: The King is dominant over His Throne.
This is supported by the saying of the poet:
'Bishr has istawa over Iraq without sword and bloodshed'
meaning: He dominated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of the slave girl contains the Prophet's exact words, so Allah must have a location.
Correction: The question 'Where is Allah?' is likely a transmission by meaning; the original hadith probably did not contain such a question, as affirming bodily location contradicts Allah's transcendence.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the hadith of the slave girl?
A) It proves that Allah is in the sky.
B) The question 'Where is Allah?' is part of the original hadith.
C) The wording is likely a result of transmission by meaning, not the Prophet's exact words.
D) The hadith is weak and should be rejected.

Key Takeaway
Transmission by meaning can introduce wording that conflicts with Allah's transcendence, so we rely on established principles of tawhid to interpret such narrations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith that seems to describe Allah with human-like qualities, do you immediately accept it literally or do you investigate its authenticity and consider the principle of tanzih? What steps can you take to guard yourself from falling into anthropomorphism?
?
The editor warns that many fell into anthropomorphism by overlooking the principle of transmission by meaning. Have you ever uncritically accepted a religious text just because it is attributed to the Prophet? How can you develop a habit of verifying narrations against the clear principles of tawhid?
?
If a friend argues that the hadith of the slave girl proves Allah is in the sky, will you be able to explain the role of transmission by meaning and the transcendence of Allah? Write down exactly what you would say to them using specific points from this lesson.

Imam Malik's Statement on Istiwa: Affirming the Attribute Without Asking How
Imam Malik's authoritative statement on istiwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Malik's normative approach to the divine attribute of istiwa, and why questioning its modality is considered an innovation.

Core Idea
We affirm the meaning, but we do not ask how.

Imam Malik's famous statement sets a clear boundary for Sunni theology: the attribute of istiwa is affirmed, its modality is beyond human comprehension, and probing into the 'how' is a sign of misguidance. This passage is a cornerstone of the Sunni approach to divine attributes, emphasizing tafwid (consigning modality to Allah) while upholding the literal meaning of the Quranic text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully. Notice the four-part structure: istiwa is not unknown, modality is not comprehensible, belief is obligatory, asking is innovation.
The harsh response to the questioner is significant.
2
Identify the key components
Break down Imam Malik's statement into its four components: what we know, what we don't know, what we must do, and what we must avoid. Also note the identification of the questioner as Jahm ibn Safwan.
3
Understand the theological significance
Reflect on why this statement is so important in Sunni creed. It establishes a middle path between denial (ta'til) and anthropomorphism (tashbih). The questioner is the founder of the Jahmiyya sect.
This statement is often cited in discussions of divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن مالك بن أنس رضي الله عنه إمام أهل المدينة أنه قال: «الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول ، والإيمان به واجب، والسؤال عنه بدعة، وقال للسائل : ما أراك إلا ضالاً. وأمره بالصفع (۱) فإذا هو جهم بن صفوان عليه اللعنة».
And from Malik ibn Anas (may Allah be pleased with him), the imam of the people of Medina, that he said: 'The istiwa is not unknown, the modality is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is an innovation.' And he said to the questioner: 'I see you are nothing but misguided.' And he ordered that he be slapped (1) and behold, it was Jahm ibn Safwan (may the curse of Allah be upon him).
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
In this brief but authoritative passage, Nasafi transmits the famous statement of Imam Malik (d. 795 CE), one of the four great Sunni imams, regarding the proper approach to the attribute of istiwa. Imam Malik's statement is a classic formulation of the Sunni stance on divine attributes: the meaning (istiwa) is known in general, but the modality (kayfiyya) is beyond human comprehension. Belief in the attribute as affirmed in the Quran is obligatory, and inquiring into its modality is an innovation (bid'a). Imam Malik considered such questioning as a sign of misguidance and dealt harshly with the questioner, who turned out to be Jahm ibn Safwan, the founder of the Jahmiyya sect. This passage underscores the principle of tafwid (consigning the modality to Allah) while affirming the attribute.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الكيف
بدعة
جهم بن صفوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Imam Malik's statement means we cannot affirm any meaning for istiwa, so we must remain completely silent about it.
Correction: Imam Malik clearly says 'al-istiwā ghayru majhūl' – the istiwa is not unknown. He affirms the meaning. The unknown is the modality, not the attribute itself.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Malik's statement, what is the ruling on asking about how istiwa occurs?
A) It is obligatory
B) It is permissible
C) It is an innovation (bid'a)
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Imam Malik's statement teaches us to affirm the divine attribute of istiwa as it is revealed, to believe in it without asking how, and to avoid speculative questioning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about divine attributes like istiwa, do you find yourself wishing to know 'how'? How does Imam Malik's statement expose the pride in your heart that wants to comprehend the incomprehensible? What would it look like for you to submit without demanding an explanation?
?
Imagine you are in a gathering where someone insists on discussing the 'mechanics' of Allah's establishment over the Throne. Will you remain silent, or will you recall Imam Malik's warning and gently redirect? What is at stake for your own faith if you tolerate that line of questioning?
?
Imam Malik did not merely correct the questioner—he declared him misguided and ordered him slapped. Are you willing to take a firm stand against theological innovation among your peers, or do you avoid conflict to maintain harmony? How does your fear of people's reactions compare to your fear of falling into innovation?

The Mu'tazila Denial of Seeing Allah and Their Proofs
Imam al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila denial of ru'ya and enumerates their scriptural proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila position on ru'ya and the three proofs they cite from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila deny the vision of Allah using three scriptural proofs.

In this chapter, Imam al-Nasafi sets the stage by stating the disagreement between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna on the possibility of seeing Allah. He then lists the evidence the Mu'tazila bring to support their denial. Understanding these proofs is essential before we examine the Sunni refutation in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Focus on the Mu'tazila claims and the three proofs they present.
Notice the word 'lan' in the verse of Moses.
2
Identify the three proofs
List the three proofs: the verse of Moses, the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar', and the hadith of Aisha.
Each proof is introduced with 'وكذلك'.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila reasoning
For each proof, consider how the Mu'tazila interpret it to deny ru'ya. The word 'lan' implies perpetual negation.
4
Reflect on the strength of these proofs
These proofs appear strong if taken literally. Think about how a Sunni scholar might respond.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في إثبات رؤية الله تعالى
قالت المعتزلة : لا تجوز الرؤية على الباري تعالى بالأبصار.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: تجوز.
وحجتهم قوله تعالى خبرا عن موسى عليه السلام: قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ قَالَ لَن تَرَننِي وكلمة (لن) للتأبيد، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ﴾.
وكذلك رُوي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت: سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «هل رأيت ربك ليلة المعراج؟ فقال: لا».
قوله تعالى: فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ فهل معنى ذلك أن المصلّي أينما ولى وجهه يكون مقابلاً لمكان الله ؟ تعالى الله عما يقولون ، وكذلك قوله: ﴿ وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ وما شابهها من آياتٍ وأخبار فإنها تُحمل على ما يليق بالله جل جلاله.
ولا يخفى فساد قول من يقول إن الله تعالى في السماء حقيقة، لأن الله تعالى قديم، والسماء محدثة محدودة، فإن كان الله في السماء بالمعنى الحقيقي فأين كان قبل أن يخلق السماء؟ ففساد هذا ظاهر لكل عاقل.
Chapter on proving the vision of Allah. The Mu'tazila said: Vision (ru'ya) of the Creator is not permissible by (physical) eyes. Ahl al-Sunna wa'l-Jama'a said: It is permissible. Their (the Mu'tazila's) proof is His statement, reporting from Moses alayhi salam: 'He said: My Lord, show me (that) I may look at You. He said: You will never see Me.' And the word 'lan' indicates perpetuity. And likewise His statement: 'Vision cannot perceive Him, and He perceives all vision.' And likewise it is narrated from A'isha radiya Allahu anha that she said: 'I asked the Messenger of Allah sallallahu alayhi wa sallam: Did you see your Lord on the night of Mi'raj? He said: No.' His statement: 'Wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah.' Does that mean that the praying person, wherever he turns his face, he faces the place of Allah? Exalted is Allah above what they say. And likewise His statement: 'And He is the One Who in the heaven is God and on the earth is God,' and similar verses and reports; they are to be interpreted as befits Allah. And it is not hidden the corruption of the statement of whoever says that Allah is truly in the heaven, because Allah is eternal, and the heaven is originated and limited. If Allah were in the heaven in a real sense, then where was He before He created the heaven? The corruption of this is clear to every rational person.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on proving the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'yat Allah) in the afterlife. The author states the Mu'tazila denial and the Sunni affirmation. Then he lists the Mu'tazila proofs: the verse of Moses with 'lan tarani' implying eternal denial, the verse 'la tudrikuhu al-absar', and the hadith of Aisha. The author then refutes these proofs by showing that the verses they cite are misinterpreted. He explains that the verse 'wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah' does not imply spatial location, nor does 'in the heaven is God' mean Allah is physically in the sky. He then refutes a literal interpretation of 'fis sama'' by arguing from Allah's eternity: since the heaven is created, if Allah were in it, where was He before its creation? This reductio shows the absurdity of corporealism.

Key Terms
رؤية
معتزلة
أهل السنة والجماعة
لن
الأبصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which word in the verse to Moses does the Mu'tazila use to argue for perpetual negation of vision?
A) 'lan'
B) 'la'
C) 'ma'
D) 'in'

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila base their denial of seeing Allah on three scriptural proofs: the verse of Moses, the verse of vision, and the hadith of Aisha.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila used the word 'lan' to claim that even Moses could not see Allah. If you were in Moses' place, would that answer satisfy your longing to see your Creator? How does your own yearning for Allah compare to that of a prophet?
?
The Prophet (saw) denied seeing his Lord on the night of Mi'raj. Does that make you doubt that you will ever see Him? Or does it increase your reliance on the Quranic promise that some faces will 'look at their Lord' (75:22-23)? What would it take for you to be certain that you will see Allah?
?
The Mu'tazila argue from Scripture, yet they arrive at a different conclusion from Ahl al-Sunna. When you read the verses they cite, do you feel the weight of their argument? How do you reconcile such texts with the hope of seeing Allah? Is your hope based on evidence or mere desire?

The Sunni Refutation of the Mu'tazila Proofs and the Argument Against Anthropomorphism
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila interpretations and disproves anthropomorphism with an argument from eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars refute the Mu'tazila proofs and why literal interpretations of certain verses are rejected.

Core Idea
The verses cited by the Mu'tazila must be interpreted in a way befitting Allah's transcendence.

After presenting the Mu'tazila evidence, Imam al-Nasafi now turns to the Sunni response. He argues that the verses and hadith they cite do not literally deny vision in the afterlife, but rather address specific contexts. Moreover, he refutes a related misconception: that Allah is physically located in heaven. This lesson shows how the same texts are interpreted consistently with tanzih.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two verses the author addresses.
2
Understand the method
The author first questions literal interpretations, then provides a rational proof. Identify both parts.
3
Follow the rational argument
Trace the argument: Allah is eternal, heaven is created. If Allah were in heaven, where was He before creation? This leads to absurdity.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Apply the principle
Generalize: all verses and reports must be interpreted in a way befitting Allah's majesty, not literally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في إثبات رؤية الله تعالى
قالت المعتزلة : لا تجوز الرؤية على الباري تعالى بالأبصار.
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: تجوز.
وحجتهم قوله تعالى خبرا عن موسى عليه السلام: قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ قَالَ لَن تَرَننِي وكلمة (لن) للتأبيد، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿لا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَرَ﴾.
وكذلك رُوي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها قالت: سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «هل رأيت ربك ليلة المعراج؟ فقال: لا».
قوله تعالى: فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ فهل معنى ذلك أن المصلّي أينما ولى وجهه يكون مقابلاً لمكان الله ؟ تعالى الله عما يقولون ، وكذلك قوله: ﴿ وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ وما شابهها من آياتٍ وأخبار فإنها تُحمل على ما يليق بالله جل جلاله.
ولا يخفى فساد قول من يقول إن الله تعالى في السماء حقيقة، لأن الله تعالى قديم، والسماء محدثة محدودة، فإن كان الله في السماء بالمعنى الحقيقي فأين كان قبل أن يخلق السماء؟ ففساد هذا ظاهر لكل عاقل.
Chapter on proving the vision of Allah. The Mu'tazila said: Vision (ru'ya) of the Creator is not permissible by (physical) eyes. Ahl al-Sunna wa'l-Jama'a said: It is permissible. Their (the Mu'tazila's) proof is His statement, reporting from Moses alayhi salam: 'He said: My Lord, show me (that) I may look at You. He said: You will never see Me.' And the word 'lan' indicates perpetuity. And likewise His statement: 'Vision cannot perceive Him, and He perceives all vision.' And likewise it is narrated from A'isha radiya Allahu anha that she said: 'I asked the Messenger of Allah sallallahu alayhi wa sallam: Did you see your Lord on the night of Mi'raj? He said: No.' His statement: 'Wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah.' Does that mean that the praying person, wherever he turns his face, he faces the place of Allah? Exalted is Allah above what they say. And likewise His statement: 'And He is the One Who in the heaven is God and on the earth is God,' and similar verses and reports; they are to be interpreted as befits Allah. And it is not hidden the corruption of the statement of whoever says that Allah is truly in the heaven, because Allah is eternal, and the heaven is originated and limited. If Allah were in the heaven in a real sense, then where was He before He created the heaven? The corruption of this is clear to every rational person.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a chapter on proving the possibility of seeing Allah (ru'yat Allah) in the afterlife. The author states the Mu'tazila denial and the Sunni affirmation. Then he lists the Mu'tazila proofs: the verse of Moses with 'lan tarani' implying eternal denial, the verse 'la tudrikuhu al-absar', and the hadith of Aisha. The author then refutes these proofs by showing that the verses they cite are misinterpreted. He explains that the verse 'wherever you turn, there is the Face of Allah' does not imply spatial location, nor does 'in the heaven is God' mean Allah is physically in the sky. He then refutes a literal interpretation of 'fis sama'' by arguing from Allah's eternity: since the heaven is created, if Allah were in it, where was He before its creation? This reductio shows the absurdity of corporealism.

Key Terms
قديم
محدثة
السماء
وجه الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that verses like 'in the heaven is God' prove Allah is physically in the sky.
Correction: The passage refutes this by showing that such a belief leads to absurdity because Allah is eternal and heaven is created.

Checkpoint
What argument does the author use to refute the literal interpretation of 'in the heaven is God'?
A) That Allah is everywhere
B) That heaven is created and Allah is eternal
C) That the verse is metaphorical
D) That the Prophet denied seeing Allah

Key Takeaway
Sunni scholars interpret verses that seem to imply spatial location in a manner consistent with Allah's transcendence, and the eternity of Allah refutes any literal indwelling in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Ahl al-Sunna's Proofs for the Vision of Allah
Sanusi enumerates several Sunni proofs for the vision of Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple proofs (Qur'anic, hadith, and rational) that Sunni scholars use to establish the possibility and occurrence of seeing Allah in the afterlife.

Core Idea
The vision of Allah is proven by the Qur'an, sunna, and rational necessity.

The Sunni school affirms that believers will see Allah in Paradise. While some deny this based on God's transcendence, the Sunnis present a range of proofs from revelation and reason. This lesson examines the key arguments from the story of Moses, explicit Qur'anic verses, and a famous hadith, showing that the vision is both possible and promised.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the five proofs presented.
Notice the recurring Arabic phrase 'وكذلك' (likewise) linking each proof.
2
Examine the proof from Musa's request
Focus on the argument that prophets are infallible (ma'sūm) and would not ask for something impossible, so Musa's request implies the vision is possible.
This is a rational proof (ḥujja 'aqliyya) based on the principle of prophetic infallibility.
3
Analyze the three Qur'anic verses
Consider each verse: 'Faces looking at their Lord', 'Hope for meeting with their Lord', and 'Whatever your souls desire'. Understand how each supports the vision.
The third verse involves a logical argument: if paradise souls desire vision, it must be granted.
4
Reflect on the hadith
The hadith compares seeing Allah to seeing the full moon without crowding, emphasizing clarity and ease.
This hadith is widely transmitted and serves as a concrete illustration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجتنا قوله تعالى خبرًا عن موسى عليه السلام: قَالَ رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنْظُرْ إِلَيْكَ فَلولا أن موسى عَلِمَ جواز رؤية الباري وإلا لما سأل، لأن الأنبياء معصومون مِنْ أن يسألوا سؤالاً مستحيلاً، وكذلك قوله تعالى: وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَيذِ نَاضِرَةٌ إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ وكذلك قوله تعالى: فَمَن كَانَ يَرْجُو القَاءَ رَبِّهِ وكذلك قوله تعالى: وَلَكُمْ فِيهَا مَا تَشْتَهِي أَنفُسُكُمْ فلو اشتهى أهل الجنة إلى الرؤية ولم يروه، يؤدي إلى الخلْفِ في كلام الله تعالى. وكذلك رُوي عن النبي أنه قال: إنكم سترون ربكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر لا تُضامُّون في رؤيته أي: لا تزاحمون في رؤيته.
And our proof is the statement of Allah, Most High, reporting from Mūsā, peace be upon him: He said: My Lord, show me (that I may) look at You. If Mūsā did not know the permissibility of seeing the Creator, he would not have asked, because the prophets are infallible from asking an impossible request. Likewise the statement of Allah, Most High: Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord. Likewise His statement: So whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord. Likewise His statement: And for you therein is whatever your souls desire. So if the people of Paradise desire the vision and do not see it, that would lead to a contradiction in the speech of Allah. And likewise it is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: You will surely see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon; you will not be harmed in seeing Him, meaning: you will not be crowded in seeing Him.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents the Sunni proofs (hujaj) for the possibility of seeing Allah. It begins with the verse of Musa: Musa asked to see Allah, and if it were impossible, he would not have asked because prophets are infallible (ma'sūm). Then it cites three verses about the afterlife: (1) 'Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord'—explicitly states looking at Allah; (2) 'Whoever hopes for the meeting with his Lord'—implies that meeting includes vision; (3) 'For you therein is whatever your souls desire'—if the people of Paradise desire vision, it must be granted, otherwise Allah's promise would be broken. Finally, it quotes the famous hadith comparing seeing Allah to seeing the full moon, with the explanation that they will not be crowded (lā tudāmūn). The passage gathers multiple proofs from reason (Musa's request) and revelation.

Key Terms
حجة
عصمة
الأنبياء
النظر إلى الله
الرؤية
لقاء الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that Allah cannot be seen because He is transcendent and the Qur'an says 'lan tarānī' (You will not see Me) to Moses.
Correction: The Sunnis argue that 'lan tarānī' was a statement to Moses in this world, not a denial of vision in the afterlife. Moreover, Moses' request itself shows that the vision is possible; otherwise a prophet would not ask for it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Musa's request a valid proof for the vision of Allah?
A) Because Allah did not punish him
B) Because prophets are infallible and do not ask for the impossible
C) Because the request was granted
D) Because it is mentioned in the Torah

Key Takeaway
The vision of Allah is established through multiple proofs: the infallibility of prophets, explicit Qur'anic verses, the principle of divine promise, and a prophetic tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about Prophet Musa (AS) asking to see Allah with such urgency, what is the most powerful longing in your life right now? How does it compare to this desire for the Divine vision, and will you ask Allah tonight to give you a similar yearning?
?
The hadith says you will see your Lord as clearly as the moon on a full moon night – without any crowding or obstacle. Does your daily life reflect a certainty in that promise, or do you live as if this world is the only reality? What one habit can you change today to live with the vision in mind?
?
If Allah promises to grant the believers whatever they desire in Paradise, including the vision of Himself, what does that say about your relationship with desires in this life? Are you training your soul to desire the highest thing, or are you settling for lesser pleasures while neglecting the ultimate aim?

The Quran: Allah's Eternal Attribute
Nasafi defines the Quran as Allah's eternal attribute and refutes the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quran is Allah's uncreated speech and attribute, distinct from created letters and sounds.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not a created thing.

Nasafi begins by affirming the Sunni position that the Quran is Allah's attribute, co-eternal with Him. He explicitly refutes the Mu'tazila who claim it is created. This foundational doctrine shapes how Muslims relate to the Quran as divine speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage from the beginning through 'neither it nor other than it' to get the definition and refutation.
Note the strong negation of createdness and physical attributes.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice that Nasafi says the Quran is Allah's speech and attribute, and that Allah with all attributes is eternal, not created.
3
Examine the refutation of Mu'tazila
The passage is explicitly a refutation of those who say the Quran is created. Understand why this distinction matters.
Mu'tazila held that the Quran is created in time.
4
Appreciate the negation of letters and sounds
Nasafi emphasizes that Allah's speech is without letters, sounds, or syllables. These are properties of created speech.
This prevents anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أن القرءان كلام الله تعالى وفيه الرد على المعتزلة. القرآن كلام الله تعالى وصفته، والله تعالى بجميع صفاته واحد قديم غير محدث ولا مخلوق، بلا حرف ولا صوت ولا مقاطع ولا مبادئ له، لا هو ولا غيره، فأسمعه جبرائيل عليه السلام بالصوت والحروف، فخلق صوتا فسمعه بذلك الصوت والحروف، فحفظه جبرائيل عليه السلام ووعاه، ونقل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إنزال الوحي والرسالة لا إنزال الشخص والصورة، وتلاه على النبي عليه السلام، فحفظه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ووعاه، وتلاه على أصحابه فحفظوه، وتلوه على التابعين، والتابعون على الصالحين، هكذا حتى وصل إلينا.
Chapter on explaining that the Quran is the speech of Allah, and in it is the refutation of the Mu'tazila. The Quran is the speech of Allah and His attribute. Allah, with all His attributes, is one, eternal, not originated nor created, without letter, without sound, without syllables, without beginning for it, neither it nor other than it. So Gabriel, peace be upon him, caused him to hear it with sound and letters. So He created a sound, and he heard it through that sound and letters. Then Gabriel, peace be upon him, preserved it and memorized it, and conveyed to the Prophet, peace be upon him, the sending down of revelation and the message, not the sending down of a person or a form. And he recited it to the Prophet, peace be upon him, so the Prophet, peace be upon him, memorized it and preserved it. And he recited it to his companions, so they memorized it. And they recited it to the successors, and the successors to the righteous, thus until it reached us.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage defines the Sunni doctrine of the Quran as the uncreated speech of Allah. Nasafi states that the Quran is Allah's attribute, and like all attributes, it is eternal, not created. He emphasizes that Allah's speech is without letters, sounds, or syllables – these are created mediums. Gabriel heard the speech through a created sound, then conveyed the meaning to the Prophet. The Prophet recited it with letters and sounds to the companions, who transmitted it. This chain preserves the Quran's divine origin while acknowledging that its physical expression is created. The passage also explicitly refutes the Mu'tazila, who held that the Quran is created.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran's letters and sounds are eternal.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the Quran as Allah's speech is without letters, sounds, or syllables; these are created mediums.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi say about the Quran's letters and sounds?
A) They are eternal.
B) They are created.
C) The Quran has no letters or sounds.
D) They are part of Allah's attribute.

Key Takeaway
The Quran is Allah's eternal speech, not created, and without physical properties like letters or sounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly internalize that you are engaging with Allah's eternal attribute—not mere words? How would your heart change if you recited with this awareness every time?
?
If the Quran is without letters and sounds in its true essence, why has Allah chosen to manifest it to us in a form we can hear? What does this say about His mercy and desire to communicate with you?
?
The Mu'tazila believed the Quran was created, perhaps to protect Allah's oneness. But have you ever, in practice, treated the Quran as a created book—like any other text—by neglecting its commands or forgetting its divine origin? What would it mean for your daily life to treat it as eternal?

How the Quran Reached Us: Gabriel's Role
Nasafi describes the transmission of the Quran from Allah through Gabriel to the Prophet and the chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the process by which Gabriel conveyed the eternal Quran to the Prophet through created sounds and letters, and the subsequent transmission chain.

Core Idea
Gabriel heard Allah's speech through a created sound and conveyed it to the Prophet.

After establishing the Quran's eternal nature, Nasafi explains how it was transmitted to humanity. He describes that Allah created a sound through which Gabriel heard the speech, then Gabriel recited it to the Prophet with letters and sounds. The Prophet then taught it to the companions, who passed it down, ensuring its preservation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on transmission
Read from 'So Gabriel...' to the end to understand the chain.
2
Understand the distinction
Note that the eternal speech was heard through a created sound and letters. This preserves the uncreated nature while allowing transmission.
3
Follow the chain
Trace the line: Allah -> Gabriel -> Prophet -> Companions -> Successors -> Us.
It is an oral transmission, not a physical object.
4
Identify what was sent down
Nasafi stresses it was the sending down of revelation and message, not a person or form.
Refutes the idea of a physical Quran descending.

The Quran is the Uncreated Speech of Allah
Nasafi defines the Quran as uncreated speech and describes its transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine that the Quran is the eternal, uncreated speech of Allah, an attribute subsisting in His essence without letters or sounds.

Core Idea
The Quran is an eternal attribute of Allah, not composed of letters or sounds.

This lesson introduces the foundational Ash'ari belief about the nature of the Quran. Imam al-Nasafi begins by affirming that the Quran is Allah’s eternal speech, an attribute subsisting in His essence, free from temporality. He also explains how this eternal speech was conveyed to the Prophet through Jibril using created sounds, and al-Taftazani’s commentary reinforces the rejection of letters/sounds as eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise definition of the Quran as an attribute.
2
Understand the definition of the Quran
Identify the key phrase: 'بلا حرف ولا صوت' – the Quran is an eternal attribute without letters or sounds. This is the core teaching.
Contrast this with the Mu'tazila view that the Quran is created.
3
Examine the transmission process
Note how Jibril heard a created sound and conveyed the meaning, not the eternal attribute itself. The chain of transmission preserves the meaning.
The eternal speech itself is never ‘brought down’; only its expression is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان أن القرءان كلام الله تعالى وفيه الرد على المعتزلة
القرآن كلام الله تعالى وصفته، والله تعالى بجميع صفاته واحد قديم غير محدث ولا مخلوق، بلا حرف ولا صوت ولا مقاطع ولا مبادئ له، لا هو ولا غيره، فأسمعه جبرائيل عليه السلام بالصوت والحروف، فخلق صوتا فسمعه بذلك الصوت والحروف، فحفظه جبرائيل عليه السلام ووعاه، ونقل إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إنزال الوحي والرسالة لا إنزال الشخص والصورة، وتلاه على النبي عليه السلام، فحفظه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ووعاه، وتلاه على أصحابه فحفظوه، وتلوه على التابعين، والتابعون على الصالحين، هكذا حتى وصل إلينا (١).
(۱) يقول السعد التفتازاني في شرحه على العقائد النسفية عن الكلام الإلهي (۱ : ۱۲۱) ما صورته ليس من جنس الحروف والأصوات ضرورةً لأنها أعراض حادثة، مشروط حدوث بعضها بانقضاء البعض؛ لأن امتناع التكلم بالحرف الثاني بدون انقضاء الحرف الأول بديهي، وفي هذا ردُّ على الحنابلة والكرامية القائلين بأن كلام الله عرَضُ من جنس الأصوات والحروف ومع ذلك هو قديم». ويقول في موضع آخر من نفس الشرح (١: ١٢٤) ما صورته: «والقرءان كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، وعقب القرءان بكلام الله تعالى لما ذكر المشايخ من أنه يقال القرءان كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ولا يقال القرءان غير مخلوق لئلا يسبق إلى الفهم أن المؤلف من الأصوات والحروف، قديم كما =
وهو مقروء بالألسن، محفوظ بالقلوب مكتوب في المصاحف وليس بموضوع في المصاحف، لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان ، حتى مَنْ أحرق المصاحف لا يحترق القرآن، كما أنَّ الله تعالى مذكور بالألسن، معروفٌ في القلوب، معبود في الأماكن، وليس بموجود في الأماكن ولا في القلوب، كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّي الَّذِى يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِندَهُمْ فِي التَّوْرَنَةِ وَالإنجيل ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٥٧] وإنما وجدوا نعته وصفته لا شَخْصَه، وكذلك الجنة والنار مذكورتان عندنا وليستا بذاتهما عندنا، هذا كله مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة.
ثم نقول: الله تعالى كلَّم جبرائيل صلوات الله عليه من وراء الحجاب، وسمع جبريل كلام الله من وراء الحجاب، وسمع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كلام الله تعالى ليلة المعراج من وراء الحجاب، وكلَّم آدم وموسى عليها السلام من وراء الحجاب.
وكلُّ مرةٍ جاء جبرائيل إلى النبي الا الله وكان ذلك بأمر الله.
ذهب إليه الحنابلة جهلاً أو عنادًا، وأقام غير مخلوق مقام غير حادث تنبيها على اتحادهما وقصدًا إلى جري الكلام على وفق الحديث، حيث قال : القرءان كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، ومن قال إنه مخلوق فهو كافر بالله العظيم، وتنصيصا على محل الخلاف بالعبارة المشهورة فيما بين الفرقتين وهو أن القرءان مخلوق أو غير مخلوق، ولهذا تترجم ا المسألة بمسألة خلق القرءان، وتحقيق الخلاف بيننا وبينهم يرجع إلى إثبات الكلام النفسي ونفيه، وإلا فنحن لا نقول بقدم الألفاظ والحروف وهم لا يقولون بحدوث الكلام النفسي. ودليلنا ما مر أنه ثبت بالإجماع وتواتر النقل عن الأنبياء صلوات الله عليهم أنه تعالى متكلم، ولا معنى له سوى أنه متصف بالكلام، ويمتنع قيام اللفظي الحادث بذاته تعالى، فتعيَّن النفسي القديم، وأما استدلالهم بأن القرءان متصف بما هو من صفات المخلوقين وسمات الحدوث من التأليف والتنظيم والإنزال والتنزيل وكونه عربيًا مسموعا فصيحا معجزًا إلى غير ذلك، فإنما يقوم حجة على الحنابلة لا علينا، لأنا قائلون بحدوث النظم، وإنما الكلام في المعنى القديم.
Chapter on explaining that the Quran is the speech of Allah the Exalted, and in it is the refutation of the Mu'tazila. The Quran is the speech of Allah the Exalted and His attribute. Allah the Exalted is one in all His attributes, eternal, not originated nor created, without letter, sound, syllables, or beginning. He is not Himself other than it. So Jibril, peace be upon him, made it heard with sound and letters, so He created a sound and he heard it with that sound and letters. Jibril, peace be upon him, memorized and preserved it, and conveyed to the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) the descent of revelation and the message, not the descent of a person or form. He recited it to the Prophet (عليه السلام), so the Prophet memorized and preserved it, recited it to his companions, so they memorized it, and they recited it to the followers, and the followers to the righteous, thus until it reached us. (1) Al-Sa'd al-Taftazani says in his commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya about the divine speech (1:121): 'It is not of the kind of letters and sounds necessarily, because they are accidental originated things, the occurrence of some of them being conditioned by the passing of others; because the impossibility of speaking the second letter without the passing of the first is self-evident. And in this is a refutation of the Hanabila and the Karamiyya who say that the speech of Allah is an accident of the kind of sounds and letters, and yet it is eternal.' And he says in another place of the same commentary (1:124): 'The Quran is the speech of Allah the Exalted, uncreated. And he appended the Quran to the speech of Allah because the shaykhs have mentioned that it is said: the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and it is not said: the Quran is uncreated, lest it come to mind that the composition of sounds and letters is eternal, just as =' And it is recited with tongues, preserved in hearts, written in mushafs, but it is not physically placed in the mushafs. It does not admit increase or decrease, so that even if one burns the mushafs, the Quran does not burn, just as Allah the Exalted is mentioned with tongues, known in hearts, worshipped in places, but He does not exist in places nor in hearts. As Allah the Exalted said: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' (Al-A'raf 157). They found only his description and attribute, not his person. Similarly, Paradise and Hell are mentioned with us but they are not themselves present with us. All this is the way of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. Then we say: Allah the Exalted spoke to Jibril, salutations of Allah upon him, from behind a veil, and Jibril heard the speech of Allah from behind a veil, and the Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) heard the speech of Allah on the night of the Mi'raj from behind a veil. And He spoke to Adam and Moses, peace be upon them, from behind a veil. And every time Jibril came to the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم), that was by Allah's command. The Hanabila went to it out of ignorance or stubbornness, and they placed 'uncreated' in the position of 'unoriginated' to indicate their unity and intending that the speech should proceed according to the hadith, where he said: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and whoever says it is created is a disbeliever in Allah the Great.' And in specifying the point of disagreement with the well-known expression between the two groups, which is that the Quran is created or uncreated, for this reason the issue is translated as the issue of the creation of the Quran. The reality of the disagreement between us and them reverts to affirming or negating internal speech. Otherwise, we do not say that the words and letters are eternal, and they do not say that internal speech is originated. Our proof is what has been established by consensus and continuous transmission from the prophets, peace be upon them, that He is speaking, and there is no meaning to that except that He is qualified by speech. And it is impossible for originated verbal speech to subsist in His essence, so internal eternal speech is determined. As for their argument that the Quran is qualified by what is among the attributes of created beings and signs of origination, such as composition, organization, descent, revelation, being Arabic, audible, eloquent, miraculous, etc., that argument holds against the Hanabila, not against us, because we affirm the origination of the composition. The discussion is only about the eternal meaning.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a composite of Imam al-Nasafi's original text and a marginal commentary by al-Taftazani. It serves as a comprehensive doctrinal statement and refutation regarding the nature of the Quran.

The passage opens with a chapter heading declaring the Quran to be Allah's speech and a refutation of the Mu'tazila. The first part of Nasafi's text affirms that the Quran is the eternal, uncreated attribute of Allah, transcending letters, sounds, syllables, or beginnings. The speech is not identical to Allah nor distinct in a way that implies multiplicity. Nasafi explains the mode of revelation: Allah created a sound that Jibril heard, allowing Jibril to memorize the speech and convey its meaning (not a physical entity) to the Prophet, who then transmitted it orally through the chain of transmission.

Al-Taftazani's footnote (interpolated) reinforces the Ash'ari position: divine speech is not composed of letters or sounds because those are originated accidents. He refutes the Hanabila and Karamiyya who affirm eternal speech of letters and sounds. Taftazani also clarifies that the phrase 'the Quran is uncreated' must be qualified as 'the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated' to avoid misunderstanding.

The main text continues with the Quran's relation to physical media: it is recited, memorized, written, but not contained in mushafs. Burning mushafs does not burn the Quran itself. An analogy with Allah's remembrance and worship shows that the referent is transcendent. A Qur'anic verse (7:157) illustrates that the Prophet was described in previous scriptures, not personally present.

Then Nasafi states the mode of divine speech: Allah spoke to Jibril, the Prophet at Mi'raj, Adam, and Moses from behind a veil, emphasizing that the speech is not directly perceived.

Finally, the passage (likely Taftazani's continuation) addresses the Hanabila's error: they conflate 'uncreated' with 'unoriginated' but the real issue is whether speech is internal (kalam nafsi) or verbal (kalam lafzi). The proof for internal eternal speech is that Allah is described as 'speaking' by consensus, and originated verbal speech cannot subsist in His essence. The opponents' arguments about the Quran's composition, organization, etc., apply to the verbal form, which Ash'aris concede is originated; the disagreement is only about the eternal meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran is identical to the written text or recited sounds.
Correction: The Quran is the eternal speech of Allah, an attribute not composed of letters or sounds; the physical forms are created means of transmission.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following describes the Quran?
A) A created composition of letters and sounds
B) The eternal, uncreated speech of Allah, an attribute subsisting in His essence
C) A physical book containing divine words
D) A sound created by Allah that Jibril heard

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, an eternal attribute, and any physical form or sound is a means of transmission, not the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you perceive it as the eternal speech of Allah that has always existed, or do you treat it like any other book? How could a shift to the former perspective transform your relationship with each verse?
?
The Mu'tazila denied the eternity of the Quran because they could not reconcile it with Allah's oneness. Is there any aspect of your belief about the Quran that you've reduced to fit your limited understanding? What would it cost you to accept the mystery of an eternal attribute?
?
If the Quran is not composed of letters or sounds in its essence, then your recitation is merely a created reflection of something far greater. Does that raise your awe when you pronounce 'Bismillah'? How can you make each recitation a conscious encounter with the eternal?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
6 min
The Quran in Recitation, Hearts, and Manuscripts
Nasafi explains the Quran's relation to physical media using analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran, as an eternal attribute, relates to its written and recited forms without being contained in them.

Core Idea
The Quran is not physically present in mushafs or voices; it is an eternal meaning.

After establishing the Quran's eternal nature, Imam al-Nasafi addresses a common confusion: how can the uncreated speech be recited, memorized, and written? He uses analogies from Allah's transcendence and a Qur'anic verse to show that the Quran is not literally located in physical objects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and the analogies
Read the passage and notice the three analogies: Quran recited by tongues, preserved in hearts, written in mushafs. Nasafi then compares this to how Allah is remembered and worshipped.
Contrast 'مقروء بالألسن' with the eternal speech itself.
2
Understand the key distinction
The Quran is not physically placed in mushafs, just as Allah is not present in places or hearts. The writing and recitation are signs, not the essence.
3
Apply the understanding
Think about the implications: burning a mushaf does not burn the Quran. This highlights the transcendence of the divine attribute.
This is a direct refutation of anthropomorphic views.

فصل في بيان أن القرءان كلام الله تعالى وفيه الرد على المعتزلة

Commentary
This passage is a composite of Imam al-Nasafi's original text and a marginal commentary by al-Taftazani. It serves as a comprehensive doctrinal statement and refutation regarding the nature of the Quran.

The passage opens with a chapter heading declaring the Quran to be Allah's speech and a refutation of the Mu'tazila. The first part of Nasafi's text affirms that the Quran is the eternal, uncreated attribute of Allah, transcending letters, sounds, syllables, or beginnings. The speech is not identical to Allah nor distinct in a way that implies multiplicity. Nasafi explains the mode of revelation: Allah created a sound that Jibril heard, allowing Jibril to memorize the speech and convey its meaning (not a physical entity) to the Prophet, who then transmitted it orally through the chain of transmission.

Al-Taftazani's footnote (interpolated) reinforces the Ash'ari position: divine speech is not composed of letters or sounds because those are originated accidents. He refutes the Hanabila and Karamiyya who affirm eternal speech of letters and sounds. Taftazani also clarifies that the phrase 'the Quran is uncreated' must be qualified as 'the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated' to avoid misunderstanding.

The main text continues with the Quran's relation to physical media: it is recited, memorized, written, but not contained in mushafs. Burning mushafs does not burn the Quran itself. An analogy with Allah's remembrance and worship shows that the referent is transcendent. A Qur'anic verse (7:157) illustrates that the Prophet was described in previous scriptures, not personally present.

Then Nasafi states the mode of divine speech: Allah spoke to Jibril, the Prophet at Mi'raj, Adam, and Moses from behind a veil, emphasizing that the speech is not directly perceived.

Finally, the passage (likely Taftazani's continuation) addresses the Hanabila's error: they conflate 'uncreated' with 'unoriginated' but the real issue is whether speech is internal (kalam nafsi) or verbal (kalam lafzi). The proof for internal eternal speech is that Allah is described as 'speaking' by consensus, and originated verbal speech cannot subsist in His essence. The opponents' arguments about the Quran's composition, organization, etc., apply to the verbal form, which Ash'aris concede is originated; the disagreement is only about the eternal meaning.

Refuting the Hanabila: Internal vs. Verbal Speech
Nasafi refutes the Hanabila by distinguishing internal from verbal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari distinction between internal speech (kalam nafsi) and verbal speech (kalam lafzi), and how it refutes the Hanabila who claim the Quran is eternal but composed of letters and sounds.

Core Idea
The Quran is uncreated because it is internal eternal speech; the verbal form is created.

In this final part, Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Hanabila (and Karamiyya) who assert that God's speech is eternal but consists of letters and sounds. He distinguishes between kalam nafsi (internal speech) and kalam lafzi (verbal expression), arguing that the former is eternal while the latter is created. He also provides a proof for the impossibility of accidental speech subsisting in God.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponents' position
Read the beginning of the passage where Nasafi describes the Hanabila's error: they equate 'uncreated' with 'unoriginated' but insist the Quran is composed of letters and sounds.
2
Understand the key distinction
Nasafi explains that the real disagreement is about internal speech (kalam nafsi) vs. verbal speech (kalam lafzi). We affirm the former as eternal; they do not.
Kalam nafsi is an attribute of Allah's essence.
3
Follow the proof
The proof: Allah is described as 'speaking' by consensus; this must be an eternal attribute because originated verbal speech cannot subsist in His essence.
This argument relies on the impossibility of accidents in Allah.
4
See how opponents' arguments backfire
The Hanabila point to the Quran's composition, but we concede that the verbal form is created. The discussion is about the eternal meaning.

Chapter on explaining that the Quran is the speech of Allah the Exalted, and in it is the refutation of the Mu'tazila. The Quran is the speech of Allah the Exalted and His attribute. Allah the Exalted is one in all His attributes, eternal, not originated nor created, without letter, sound, syllables, or beginning. He is not Himself other than it. So Jibril, peace be upon him, made it heard with sound and letters, so He created a sound and he heard it with that sound and letters. Jibril, peace be upon him, memorized and preserved it, and conveyed to the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) the descent of revelation and the message, not the descent of a person or form. He recited it to the Prophet (عليه السلام), so the Prophet memorized and preserved it, recited it to his companions, so they memorized it, and they recited it to the followers, and the followers to the righteous, thus until it reached us. (1) Al-Sa'd al-Taftazani says in his commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya about the divine speech (1:121): 'It is not of the kind of letters and sounds necessarily, because they are accidental originated things, the occurrence of some of them being conditioned by the passing of others; because the impossibility of speaking the second letter without the passing of the first is self-evident. And in this is a refutation of the Hanabila and the Karamiyya who say that the speech of Allah is an accident of the kind of sounds and letters, and yet it is eternal.' And he says in another place of the same commentary (1:124): 'The Quran is the speech of Allah the Exalted, uncreated. And he appended the Quran to the speech of Allah because the shaykhs have mentioned that it is said: the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and it is not said: the Quran is uncreated, lest it come to mind that the composition of sounds and letters is eternal, just as =' And it is recited with tongues, preserved in hearts, written in mushafs, but it is not physically placed in the mushafs. It does not admit increase or decrease, so that even if one burns the mushafs, the Quran does not burn, just as Allah the Exalted is mentioned with tongues, known in hearts, worshipped in places, but He does not exist in places nor in hearts. As Allah the Exalted said: 'Those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered prophet, whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel' (Al-A'raf 157). They found only his description and attribute, not his person. Similarly, Paradise and Hell are mentioned with us but they are not themselves present with us. All this is the way of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. Then we say: Allah the Exalted spoke to Jibril, salutations of Allah upon him, from behind a veil, and Jibril heard the speech of Allah from behind a veil, and the Messenger of Allah (صلى الله عليه وسلم) heard the speech of Allah on the night of the Mi'raj from behind a veil. And He spoke to Adam and Moses, peace be upon them, from behind a veil. And every time Jibril came to the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم), that was by Allah's command. The Hanabila went to it out of ignorance or stubbornness, and they placed 'uncreated' in the position of 'unoriginated' to indicate their unity and intending that the speech should proceed according to the hadith, where he said: 'The Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated, and whoever says it is created is a disbeliever in Allah the Great.' And in specifying the point of disagreement with the well-known expression between the two groups, which is that the Quran is created or uncreated, for this reason the issue is translated as the issue of the creation of the Quran. The reality of the disagreement between us and them reverts to affirming or negating internal speech. Otherwise, we do not say that the words and letters are eternal, and they do not say that internal speech is originated. Our proof is what has been established by consensus and continuous transmission from the prophets, peace be upon them, that He is speaking, and there is no meaning to that except that He is qualified by speech. And it is impossible for originated verbal speech to subsist in His essence, so internal eternal speech is determined. As for their argument that the Quran is qualified by what is among the attributes of created beings and signs of origination, such as composition, organization, descent, revelation, being Arabic, audible, eloquent, miraculous, etc., that argument holds against the Hanabila, not against us, because we affirm the origination of the composition. The discussion is only about the eternal meaning.

Commentary
This passage is a composite of Imam al-Nasafi's original text and a marginal commentary by al-Taftazani. It serves as a comprehensive doctrinal statement and refutation regarding the nature of the Quran.

The passage opens with a chapter heading declaring the Quran to be Allah's speech and a refutation of the Mu'tazila. The first part of Nasafi's text affirms that the Quran is the eternal, uncreated attribute of Allah, transcending letters, sounds, syllables, or beginnings. The speech is not identical to Allah nor distinct in a way that implies multiplicity. Al-Taftazani's footnote (interpolated) reinforces the Ash'ari position: divine speech is not composed of letters or sounds because those are originated accidents. He refutes the Hanabila and Karamiyya who affirm eternal speech of letters and sounds. Taftazani also clarifies that the phrase 'the Quran is uncreated' must be qualified as 'the Quran is the speech of Allah, uncreated' to avoid misunderstanding.

The main text continues with the Quran's relation to physical media: it is recited, memorized, written, but not contained in mushafs. Burning mushafs does not burn the Quran itself. An analogy with Allah's remembrance and worship shows that the referent is transcendent. A Qur'anic verse (7:157) illustrates that the Prophet was described in previous scriptures, not personally present.

Then Nasafi states the mode of divine speech: Allah spoke to Jibril, the Prophet at Mi'raj, Adam, and Moses from behind a veil, emphasizing that the speech is not directly perceived.

Finally, the passage (likely Taftazani's continuation) addresses the Hanabila's error: they conflate 'uncreated' with 'unoriginated' but the real issue is whether speech is internal (kalam nafsi) or verbal (kalam lafzi). The proof for internal eternal speech is that Allah is described as 'speaking' by consensus, and originated verbal speech cannot subsist in His essence. The opponents' arguments about the Quran's composition, organization, etc., apply to the verbal form, which Ash'aris concede is originated; the disagreement is only about the eternal meaning.

The Locus Argument: Why the Quran is Uncreated
Ahl al-Sunna's proof that the Quran is uncreated via dichotomy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna proof that the Quran is uncreated based on the impossibility of it being a locus for originated things.

Core Idea
The Quran cannot be created because its creation would make Allah's essence like a created being.

The question of whether the Quran is created or uncreated was a major theological controversy. This passage presents a crisp dichotomous proof from Ahl al-Sunna: if the Quran were created, it would have to be created either outside or inside Allah's essence. Both options lead to absurd conclusions, forcing the conclusion that the Quran is uncreated.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the argument's two-part structure.
The proof uses a dichotomy (either/or) to eliminate possibilities.
2
Examine the first branch
Consider the scenario where the Quran is created outside Allah's essence. The author argues that would make that external thing the speaker, which is absurd because speech must inhere in the speaker.
The analogy of 'black' and 'red' illustrates that attributes belong to the subject.
3
Examine the second branch
Consider the scenario where the Quran is created within Allah's essence. The author argues that would make Allah's essence a locus for originated events (hawadith), which would imply resemblance to created beings.
This is negated by the Qur'anic verse 'There is nothing like unto Him.'
4
Draw the conclusion
Since both branches lead to impossible outcomes, the original assumption that the Quran is created must be false. Therefore, the Quran is uncreated.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحجة أهل السنة والجماعة في أن كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق، لأنه لو كان مخلوقا لا يخلو إما أن خَلَقَه في غير ذاته أو في ذاته، فإن كان مخلوقا في غير ذاته لكان المتكلم ذلك الذات، لأن المتكلم من قام به صفة الكلام، كالأسود والأحمر اسم لشخص قام به صفةُ السواد والحُمْرة، ولا وجة إلى أن خَلَقَه في ذاته؛ لأنه حينئذ تكون ذاته محلاً للحوادث، فيكون ذاته شبيها بذوات المخلوقين ومثلهم، وإنه منفي بقوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ﴾ [الشورى: ١١]
And the proof of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a that the speech of Allah is not created: because if it were created, it would not be free from [the possibility] that He created it outside His essence or in His essence. If it were created outside His essence, then that essence would be the speaker, because the speaker is the one in whom the attribute of speech resides, just as 'black' and 'red' are names for a person in whom the attribute of blackness or redness resides. And there is no way that He created it in His essence, because then His essence would be a locus for originated things (mahallan lil-hawadith), so His essence would resemble the essences of created beings and be like them, and that is negated by His saying: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing.'
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a proof from Ahl al-Sunna that the Quran is uncreated. The proof is based on a dichotomy: if the Quran were created, either it was created outside of Allah's essence (i.e., as a separate created thing) or within His essence. If outside, then the locus of creation (that essence) would be the speaker, but that is absurd because the speaker is the one who possesses the attribute of speech, not a separate created thing. If inside His essence, then His essence would be a locus for originated events, making Him similar to creatures, which is negated by the verse. Thus, the Quran must be uncreated.

Key Terms
كلام الله
مخلوق
ذات
محل للحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'outside His essence' could refer to a separate created thing being the speaker, implying the Quran could be created as a separate entity that is still called 'speech of Allah'.
Correction: The proof shows that if the Quran were created outside Allah's essence, that created entity would have to be the speaker (since speech inheres in it), but the speaker is Allah, not the created entity. Thus, the Quran cannot be a separate created thing.

Checkpoint

A) His essence would be the speaker
B) His essence would be a locus for originated things
C) His essence would be like created beings
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Quran is uncreated because if it were created, it would have to be either outside or inside Allah's essence, both of which are impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The proof argues that Allah's speech cannot be separated from His essence. When you recite the Quran, do you truly feel you are encountering Allah Himself, or do you sometimes treat it as a mere book?
?
Consider the verse 'There is nothing like unto Him.' Does your heart fully accept that Allah is beyond all comparison, even in how you imagine Him? What would need to shift in your worship for this to be real?

Commanding the Nonexistent: Response to an Objection
A refutation of the objection that an uncreated Quran implies commanding nonexistent things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why commanding the nonexistent does not contradict the uncreatedness of the Quran, and how the author uses analogies from divine attributes to support his argument.

Core Idea
Commanding the nonexistent is no more problematic than Allah knowing or hearing what does not yet exist.

This lesson addresses a common objection against the uncreated Quran: if it is eternal, then it would involve commanding things that do not yet exist. The author responds by clarifying the nature of divine command and drawing an analogy with Allah's eternal attributes. We will examine the objection, the reply, and the supporting analogy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the passage where the objector claims that an uncreated Quran would entail commanding the nonexistent. Notice the opponent's reasoning.
The objection assumes commands require an existing addressee.
2
Examine the author's reply
Identify how the author argues that commanding the nonexistent is permissible as a future-directed command. The command is given in pre-eternity but takes effect at a specific time.
The author says: 'He said to things: Be at such-and-such a time.'
3
See the analogy with divine attributes
Read the analogy with hearing, knowledge, and sight. Allah knows all things eternally, even before they exist. Similarly, He commands before the objects exist.
The analogy shows that eternal attributes do not require contemporaneous objects.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Consider how this passage upholds the eternity of divine attributes and the permissibility of addressing commands to future entities.
This is a standard Ash'ari defense against the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله: «لو قلنا بأنَّ كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق لكان أمرًا وناهيا للمعدوم». قلنا: [المعدومات] يجوز أن تؤمر عندنا على معنى أنه قال للأشياء: كوني في وقت كذا، ويجوز أن الله تعالى قال للأشياء قبل أن تكون كوني في وقت كذا وكذا. ولا يلزم ما قلتم كالسمع والعلم والبصر ، فإنه عالم في الأزل بجميع المعلومات، سميع بجميع المسموعات، بصير بجميع المبصرات، وإن لم تكن المسموعات والمعلومات والمبصرات موجودة في الأزل، وأنه يسمع عند وجود المسموعات بسمعه القديم القائم بالذات الأزلي في الأزل، وكذا البصر.
As for his saying: 'If we say that the speech of Allah is uncreated, then He would be commanding and prohibiting the nonexistent.' We say: [Nonexistent things] can be commanded in our view, meaning that He said to things: 'Be' at such-and-such a time. And it is permissible that Allah said to things before they existed: 'Be at such-and-such a time.' And what you have said does not follow, just as hearing, knowledge, and sight [do not follow]. For He is knowledgeable in pre-eternity of all known things, hearing of all heard things, seeing of all seen things, even if the heard things, known things, and seen things did not exist in pre-eternity. And He hears upon the existence of heard things with His eternal hearing subsisting in the essence, eternal in pre-eternity, and likewise sight.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent argues that if the Quran is uncreated and eternal, then Allah would be commanding and prohibiting things that do not yet exist, which is irrational. The author replies that commanding the nonexistent is permissible in the sense that Allah said 'Be' at a specific time for things to come into existence. He draws an analogy with the attributes of knowledge, hearing, and sight: Allah knows all things eternally even before they exist, and He hears and sees when they exist with His eternal attributes. So commanding the nonexistent is no more problematic than knowing the nonexistent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An eternal Quran would require Allah to give commands to beings that do not yet exist, which is absurd.
Correction: Commanding the nonexistent is possible as a future-directed decree, analogous to Allah's eternal knowledge of future events.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the objection that an uncreated Quran would entail commanding the nonexistent?
A) The command is directed at the nonexistent as if it existed
B) Commanding the nonexistent is permissible because the command is directed at the thing in a specific future time
C) The Quran is not actually a command
D) The objection is invalid because God only commands what will exist immediately

Key Takeaway
The author refutes the objection by showing that commanding the nonexistent is analogous to Allah's eternal knowledge, hearing, and sight, all of which are directed at future objects.

?
The objector thought that commanding the nonexistent was absurd. Are there areas in your life where you doubt Allah's ability to direct what is not yet visible—like your future or change in your heart? How does this lesson expose that doubt?

Opponent's Quranic Arguments for the Createdness of the Quran
Opponent cites five Quranic verses to argue the Quran is created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five Quranic verses that opponents use to argue that the Quran is created, and the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Opponents use explicit Quranic words to claim the Quran is created.

In theological debates, both sides appeal to the Quran. Here, the opponent presents five verses that seem to describe the Quran as newly originated, made, or subject to preservation and removal. These are their key textual proofs. Understanding them is essential before studying the response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice the pattern: each verse is cited and then interpreted as implying creation.
2
Identify the five verses
List the five Quranic verses and the key word that the opponent uses to argue for createdness (محدث, مجعول, في الصدور, حفظ, ذهاب).
3
Examine the opponent's reasoning
For each verse, understand the logical link: e.g., everything muhdath is makhluq. Ask yourself if the link is necessarily valid.
4
Note the absence of response
Remember that this passage only presents the objections. The author's counter-arguments are not here. This lesson focuses on understanding the opponent's case.
5
Reflect on the method
The opponent uses linguistic analysis and theological principles. Consider how a mutakallim might respond to each claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: ههنا دلائل أُخَرُ تدل على أنَّ كلام الله تعالى مخلوق، منها: قوله تعالى: ما يأتيهم من ذِكْرِ مِن رَّبِّهِم تُحْدَثٍ إِلَّا اسْتَمَعُوهُ وَهُمْ يَلْعَبُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢] وكلُّ محدَثٍ مخلوق، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّا جَعَلْنَهُ قُرْءَ انَّا عَرَبِيًّا * وكل مجعول مخلوق. وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ بَلْ هُوَ ايَتْ بَيِّنَتُ فِي صُدُورِ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْعِلْمَ ﴾ [العنكبوت: ٤٩] وما في صدور يكون مخلوقا، وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا الذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُ لحَفِظُونَ ﴾ [الحجر: ٩] وكذلك [قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَين شِئْنَا لَنَذْهَبَنَّ بِالَّذِي أَوْحَيْنَا إلَيْكَ )] [الإسراء: ٨٦] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّا عَلَى ذَهَابِ بِهِ لَقَدِرُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ۱۸] وما يحتاج إلى الحفظ يكون مخلوقا، وما يُذهبُ به يكون مخلوقا.
For it is said: Here are other evidences indicating that the speech of Allah is created. Among them: His saying: 'There does not come to them a new reminder (dhikr muhdath) from their Lord except that they listen to it while they play' (21:2). And everything newly originated is created. Likewise His saying: 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran' (43:3). And everything made is created. Likewise His saying: 'Rather, it is clear verses in the breasts of those who have been given knowledge' (29:49). And what is in breasts is created. Likewise His saying: 'Indeed, We sent down the Reminder, and indeed We will preserve it' (15:9). Likewise His saying: 'And if We willed, We could surely take away that which We have revealed to you' (17:86). And His saying: 'And indeed We are able to take it away' (23:18). And what needs preservation is created, and what can be taken away is created.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents the opponent's objections using Quranic verses to argue that the Quran is created. The opponent cites: 1) The term 'muhdath' (new, originated) applied to the Quran implies it is created. 2) The verb 'ja'ala' (made/jal) implies creation. 3) The Quran is in the breasts of people, which is a created place. 4) The Quran is sent down and preserved, and what is sent down is created. 5) The Quran can be taken away, indicating it is created. Note: The author's response to these objections is not included in this passage; this is the end of the page. Therefore, this lesson is incomplete.
