The Name and the Named Are One
Nasafi states the Ahl al-Sunna position and provides Quranic and rational proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position that the name and the named are identical, and the Quranic and rational proofs for this view.

Core Idea
The name of Allah is not a separate created thing; it refers to His very essence.

This lesson presents the foundational Sunni doctrine that Allah's names are not distinct from His essence. Imam Nasafi states the position, cites Quranic evidence, and uses everyday legal examples to show that names refer directly to their referents.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement and opposing view
Read the passage from the beginning up to the mention of the Mu'tazila and Mutashabbiha. Notice the clear contrast between the two positions.
The opposed view is that names are created and separate from Allah.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
The author uses the verse 'So call upon Allah, being sincere to Him in religion.' Consider why this verse proves that calling upon Allah means calling upon His essence, not a separate name.
The verse commands sincerity to Allah, not to a name.
3
Examine the legal analogies
Look at the examples of divorce, emancipation, and marriage. These everyday legal acts show that names refer to real entities; otherwise, these acts would have no effect.
If 'name' were separate, saying 'his wife is divorced' would not divorce the actual wife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان حقيقة الاسم والمسمى اعلم بأن الاسم والمسمّى واحد عن أهل السنة والجماعة، والله تعالى بجميع أسمائه وقالت المعتزلة والمتقشفة: إن اسم الله تعالى غير الله تعالى، وهو مخلوق. دليلنا قوله تعالى: ﴿فَادْعُوا اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَ﴾ [غافر: ١٤] [وقوله وَمَا أَمرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُوا اللهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الذِينَ] [البينة ] الله تعالى أمرنا أن نوحد الله، فلو كان اسم الله تعالى غير الله تعالى، لكان حصول التوحيد للاسم لا الله تعالى، وليس المقصود منه الألف واللام والهاء، وإنما المقصود هو الله تعالى، وهو كقوله تعالى: ﴿يَنيَحْيَى خُذِ الْكِتَبَ بِقُوَّق [مريم: ۱۲] لم يُرِدْ به الاسم. وكذلك لو قال: عبده حر، وامرأته طالق. يقع الطلاق والعتاق، فلو كان الاسم غير المسمّى لا يقع الطلاق والعتاق، وكذلك لو تزوج امرأة يصح النكاح على المسمى، فلو كان الاسم غير المسمَّى لكان وقوع النكاح على الاسم دون المسمى. فإن قيل : رُويَ عن النبي الله أنه قال: «إن الله تسعة وتسعين اسماً من أحصاها دخل الجنة». فلو كان الاسم والمسمّى واحداً لكان تسعةً وتسعين إلها وهذا محال، وكذلك لو قال الرجل: «النار» فلو كان الاسم والمسمى واحداً لاحترق فمه، وكذلك لو كتب اسم الله تعالى على النجاسة فلو كان كما قلتم؛ لكان يوجد ذات الله تعالى على النجاسة وهذا محال. قلنا : اسم الشيء يدل على عين ذلك الشيء. ومعنى الخبر أنه أراد به التسميات وفَرْقُ بين الاسم والتسمية؛ لأن أهلَ كلّ لغة يسمونه بلغة نحو: الهند، والسند، والترك، والعرب والعجم، والتسميات والعبارات مختلفة والله تعالى واحد، كما أن الشخص الواحد يقال له: زَيدٌ عالم فاضل صالح فَقِيةٌ، كذلك ههنا، وكل اسم إذا سمَّيته فهو الله. وأما ما ذكرتم من النار . قلنا: إنما لم يحترق فمه لأنه وجد منه تسمية النار لا حقيقة النار، وأما إذا كتب اسم الله تعالى على النجاسة. قلنا ذلك كتابة وتسمية ولم توجد ذات الله تعالى على النجاسة.
Chapter on explaining the reality of the name and the named. Know that the name and the named are one according to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, and Allah Most High with all His names. And the Mu'tazila and the Mutashabbiha said: The name of Allah Most High is other than Allah Most High, and it is created. Our proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So call upon Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' [Ghafir: 14] [and His saying: 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' (al-Bayyinah)]. Allah Most High commanded us to declare the oneness of Allah. So if the name of Allah Most High were other than Allah Most High, then the attainment of tawhid would be for the name, not for Allah Most High. And what is intended by it is not the alif, lam, and ha', but what is intended is Allah Most High. And it is like His saying: 'O Yahya, take the Book with strength' [Maryam: 12]—He did not intend the name. And likewise, if one says: 'His slave is free,' or 'His wife is divorced,' divorce and emancipation occur. So if the name were other than the named, divorce and emancipation would not occur. And likewise, if one marries a woman, the marriage contract is valid based on the named (mahr). So if the name were other than the named, then the marriage would occur on the name, not on the named. If it is said: It is narrated from the Prophet (SAW) that he said: 'Allah has ninety-nine names; whoever enumerates them enters Paradise.' So if the name and the named were one, then there would be ninety-nine gods, and this is impossible. And likewise, if a man says: 'Fire,' then if the name and the named were one, his mouth would burn. And likewise, if the name of Allah Most High is written on impurity, then if it were as you claim, the essence of Allah Most High would exist on impurity, and this is impossible. We say: The name of a thing indicates the essence of that thing. And the meaning of the hadith is that He intended by it the [acts of] naming. And there is a difference between the name and naming; because the people of every language name Him in their language, like Hindi, Sindhi, Turk, Arab, and non-Arab. The namings and expressions differ, but Allah Most High is one. Just as a single person is called 'Zayd,' 'scholar,' 'virtuous,' 'righteous,' 'jurist,' likewise here. And every name, when you name it, it is Allah. As for what you mentioned about fire: We say that his mouth did not burn only because what occurred from him was the naming of fire, not the reality of fire. And as for writing the name of Allah on impurity: We say that is writing and naming, and the essence of Allah Most High did not exist on impurity.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument establishing the position of Ahl al-Sunna that the name (ism) and the named (musamma) are one and the same, specifically regarding Allah's names. It begins by stating the Ahl al-Sunna creed that the name and the named are one, and that Allah is one with all His names. Then it presents the opposing view of the Mu'tazila and the Mutashabbiha (or Mutafalsifa), who claim that the name of Allah is other than Allah and is created. The author then provides proofs from the Quran and rational analogy. The first proof is from the Quranic command to call upon Allah sincerely; if the name were other than Allah, then calling upon the name would not constitute worship of Allah. The verse intends the essence, not the letters alif-lam-ha'. Similarly, the Quranic address to Yahya (AS) 'take the Book with strength' intends the person, not the name. The second proof is from everyday speech: if a master says 'his slave is free' or 'his wife is divorced', the legal effects follow because the name refers to the actual person. If the name were separate, those effects would not occur. Similarly, in marriage the contract is on the named (the mahr), not on the word. Then an objection is raised: the Prophet (SAW) said Allah has ninety-nine names; if name and named were one, that would imply ninety-nine gods. Also, if someone says 'fire', their mouth should burn; and writing Allah's name on impurity would place His essence on impurity. The answer distinguishes between the name and the act of naming (tasmiya). The name indicates the essence, but the ninety-nine names are different expressions (tasmiyat) for the same essence, just as a single person can be described with many attributes. The fire example: saying 'fire' is just naming, not producing fire. Writing the name is a representation, not the essence itself. Thus the objections are refuted, and the Ahl al-Sunna position is upheld.

Key Terms
اسم
مسمى
توحيد
أهل السنة والجماعة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The name of Allah is a created entity distinct from Allah.
Correction: The name is identical to the named in reference; it is not created. The name indicates the essence itself.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Ahl al-Sunna on the name and the named?
A) They are separate.
B) They are one.
C) The name is created.
D) The named is created.

Key Takeaway
The name of Allah is not a separate entity; it refers directly to Allah's essence, as proven by Quranic commands and legal practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Allah' in your prayers, do you truly feel you are addressing the Living, Eternal Essence, or is it just a word you say out of habit? If it were a mere label, would your heart still be satisfied?
?
If the name 'Allah' were created and separate, your worship would be directed at something other than God. Does that thought shake you? Are you absolutely certain that the One you call upon is present in your invocation?
?
The author uses everyday examples like divorce and freeing a slave to show that names refer to real beings. In your own life, when you use the name 'Allah' in oaths or supplications, do you treat it as a serious reference to a real Person, or do you let your tongue speak while your heart is absent?

Answering Objections: Name vs. Naming
Nasafi presents three objections and answers them by distinguishing name from naming.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes objections from the hadith of 99 names and from the examples of fire and impurity by distinguishing between the name and the act of naming.

Core Idea
The ninety-nine names are different names for one God, just as one person has many descriptions.

This lesson covers the objections raised against the unity of name and named, and Nasafi's decisive answers. He explains that the ninety-nine names refer to the same essence, that saying 'fire' is not the same as experiencing fire, and that writing the name is not the essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the three objections
Read the objections from the hadith of 99 names, the fire example, and the impurity example. Notice how each objection tries to show absurd consequences of the doctrine.
The objections assume that if name and named are one, then multiple names mean multiple gods, etc.
2
Understand the key distinction: ism vs. tasmiya
Nasafi answers by distinguishing between the name (ism) and the act of naming (tasmiya). The hadith refers to tasmiyat, different linguistic expressions for the same God.
This distinction resolves the apparent multiplicity.
3
Analyze the analogy of a person with many attributes
Just as one person can be called Zayd, scholar, virtuous, etc., so Allah has many names but is one. Consider how this analogy clarifies the unity.
The attributes do not multiply the essence.
4
Examine the answers to fire and impurity
For the fire objection, saying 'fire' is just naming, not producing fire. For impurity, writing the name is a representation, not the essence.
These answers preserve the transcendence of Allah.

?

Let this lesson free you from such confusion and direct your reverence solely to Allah's essence.

Allah's Names: Name and Named
Nasafi answers the objection that Allah's names imply multiple gods if name equals named.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between Allah's names (asmā') and His essence, and why multiple names do not imply multiple gods.

Core Idea
A single essence can have many names without multiplication.

In this lesson, Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection: if Allah's name is identical to His essence, then His ninety-nine names would mean ninety-nine gods. He clarifies the relationship between name (ism), named (musammā), and naming (tasmiya), showing how multiple names point to one Being.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the three hypothetical problems raised: the hadith of 99 names, the word 'fire', and writing Allah's name on impurity. Understand why someone would think name equals named.
2
Understand the answer
Nasafi distinguishes between ism (name) and tasmiya (naming). The name indicates the essence but is not identical to it; the naming is the linguistic expression. Note how he uses the example of a single person having multiple descriptions.
Key point: The hadith refers to tasmiat (namings), not separate essences.
3
Apply the principle
See how the same logic resolves each objection: uttering 'fire' is a naming, not the reality; writing Allah's name is a written naming, not His essence. Conclude that the distinction preserves tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : رُويَ عن النبي الله أنه قال: «إن الله تسعة وتسعين اسماً من أحصاها دخل الجنة». فلو كان الاسم والمسمّى واحداً لكان تسعةً وتسعين إلها وهذا محال، وكذلك لو قال الرجل: «النار» فلو كان الاسم والمسمى واحداً لاحترق فمه، وكذلك لو كتب اسم الله تعالى على النجاسة فلو كان كما قلتم؛ لكان يوجد ذات الله تعالى على النجاسة وهذا محال. قلنا : اسم الشيء يدل على عين ذلك الشيء. ومعنى الخبر أنه أراد به التسميات وفَرْقُ بين الاسم والتسمية؛ لأن أهلَ كلّ لغة يسمونه بلغة نحو: الهند، والسند، والترك، والعرب والعجم، والتسميات والعبارات مختلفة والله تعالى واحد، كما أن الشخص الواحد يقال له: زَيدٌ عالم فاضل صالح فَقِيةٌ، كذلك ههنا، وكل اسم إذا سمَّيته فهو الله. وأما ما ذكرتم من النار . قلنا: إنما لم يحترق فمه لأنه وجد منه تسمية النار لا حقيقة النار، وأما إذا كتب اسم الله تعالى على النجاسة. قلنا ذلك كتابة وتسمية ولم توجد ذات الله تعالى على النجاسة.
If it is said: It is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'Indeed Allah has ninety-nine names; whoever enumerates them enters Paradise.' So if the name and the named were one, then there would be ninety-nine gods, and this is impossible. Likewise, if a man says 'the fire', then if the name and the named were one, his mouth would burn. Likewise, if the name of Allah Almighty is written on impurity, then if it were as you claim, the essence of Allah Almighty would be present on impurity, and this is impossible. We say: The name of a thing indicates the essence of that thing. The meaning of the hadith is that he intended by it the namings (tasmiyat), and there is a difference between the name (ism) and the naming (tasmiya). Because the people of every language name Him in their language, such as Hindi, Sindhi, Turkish, Arab, and non-Arab. The namings and expressions are different while Allah Almighty is one, just as a single person is called Zayd, scholar, virtuous, righteous, jurist — likewise here. And every name, when you name with it, it is Allah. As for what you mentioned about fire, we say: His mouth does not burn only because he produced the naming of fire, not the reality of fire. As for writing the name of Allah on impurity, we say: That is writing and naming, and the essence of Allah Almighty is not present on impurity.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit dealing with the relationship between Allah's names and His essence. The objector raises three hypothetical problems if the name (ism) and the named (musamma) were identical: (1) the hadith listing 99 names would imply 99 gods; (2) uttering the word 'fire' would burn the mouth; (3) writing Allah's name on impure substances would bring His essence into contact with impurity. The answer explains that the name indicates the essence of the thing but is not identical to it; there is a distinction between the name itself (ism) and the act of naming (tasmiya). The hadith refers to the various namings (tasmiat) across languages, while the Named (Allah) is one. Similarly, a single person can have multiple descriptive names. Uttering 'fire' is a naming, not the reality, so no burning. Writing Allah's name is a written naming, not His essence. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
اسم
مسمى
تسمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many people think that Allah's names are identical to His essence, leading to the idea of multiple gods.
Correction: Nasafi explains that names are expressions (tasmiat) indicating the essence, not the essence itself.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the difference between the name (ism) and the naming (tasmiya)?
A) They are identical.
B) The name is the essence, the naming is the expression.
C) The name is the expression, the naming is the essence.
D) There is no difference.

Key Takeaway
Allah's many names do not imply many gods; names are linguistic expressions (tasmiat) that refer to a single, unique Essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Beautiful Names of Allah, do you sometimes feel that each name refers to a different god or deity? How does this lesson's distinction between name and naming reshape your understanding of tawheed when you say 'Ya Rahman, Ya Raheem'? What will you do the next time you recite Asma ul-Husna to ensure your heart affirms the oneness?
?
Think of a moment when you saw the name of Allah written in a place you considered disrespectful. Did your emotional reaction stem from treating the name as the Essence itself, or from respect for the One it points to? How should this lesson change your response to such situations?
?
The objector thought that saying 'fire' would burn the mouth if name equaled named. Have you ever acted as if uttering Allah's name has a magical or automatic effect, forgetting that it is a naming (tasmiya) not the reality? In what specific area of your worship or daily life do you need to realign your heart to focus on the Named (Allah) rather than the words themselves?

When Obedience Leads to Shirk: Answering an Objection
Nasafi refutes objection by specifying obedience in shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the claim that obeying a sinner in permissible matters constitutes shirk by specifying the context of the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
Obedience becomes shirk only when the command itself involves shirk, not in neutral matters.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi addresses a common objection: doesn't the Quran say that obeying certain people makes you a polytheist? He clarifies that the verse refers specifically to obeying them in their false beliefs about what God has made lawful or unlawful. This lesson unpacks his argument and its implications for understanding the limits of obedience and sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the objector's citation of the Quranic verse.
2
Identify the objection and the response
The objector uses the verse to argue that any obedience to a sinner is shirk. Find where Imam Nasafi responds (قلنا) and how he specifies the meaning.
The response begins with 'قلنا'.
3
Understand the historical context
The author provides a concrete example: the polytheists' claim about carrion. See how this example clarifies the type of obedience meant.
The context shows that the obedience was in a religious ruling, not a neutral act.
4
Apply the principle
Ask yourself: Does obeying a sinner in permissible matters (like food choices) amount to shirk? Use the passage to answer.
The key is whether the obedience is in an act of shirk itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ أَطَعْتُمُوهُمْ إِنَّكُمْ لَمَشْرِكُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١٢] قلنا: المراد به الطاعة في الشرك؛ لأنهم قالوا: الميتة حلال؛ لأنه مذبوح الله تعالى، فأنزل الله تعالى هذه الآية: وَلَا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذكر أسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ۱۱۲]
As for His saying, Exalted is He: 'And if you obey them, indeed you are polytheists' (Al-An'am 6:112), we say: the intended meaning is obedience in shirk, because they said: 'Carrion is lawful because it is slaughtered by Allah,' so Allah, Exalted is He, revealed this verse: 'And do not eat of that upon which the name of Allah has not been mentioned' (Al-An'am 6:112).
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage deals with an objection. The objector cites the verse 'And if you obey them, indeed you are polytheists' to argue that any compliance with a sinful person's opinion constitutes shirk, implying that a major sinner's rule should not be followed. The author (Imam Nasafi) responds (qulnā) by specifying that the verse refers to obedience in shirk itself, not in general matters. He provides context: the polytheists claimed that dead animals (maytah) are lawful because they were killed by Allah, implying that the name of Allah has been mentioned upon them. In response, Allah revealed the prohibition of eating meat not slaughtered in His name. Therefore, those who obeyed that opinion were committing shirk. But obedience to a sinner in permissible or neutral matters does not amount to shirk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any obedience to a sinner, even in permissible matters, makes one a polytheist.
Correction: The Quranic verse about obedience leading to shirk is limited to obedience in acts of shirk themselves, not in neutral or permissible acts.

Checkpoint

A) Obedience in matters of trade
B) Obedience in acts of shirk
C) Obedience in prayer
D) Obedience in family matters

Key Takeaway
The verse about obedience leading to shirk is context-specific; only obeying someone in an act of shirk itself constitutes polytheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Consider your daily interactions: are there any compromises you make in obedience to authority—whether parents, teachers, or community leaders—that might border on shirk? What would it take for you to stop and say, 'This command involves something contrary to Allah's oneness, and I cannot obey'?

Kasb and Tawakkul: Inner Reliance and Outward Effort
Begins the Sunni refutation that kasb contradicts tawakkul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tawakkul (trust in God) is an inner state of the heart that does not negate lawful acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
Tawakkul is a quality of the heart, not a prohibition of action.

In this passage, the author directly confronts the claim that seeking a livelihood (kasb) violates trust in God (tawakkul). He defines tawakkul as a heart-based reliance on God, distinct from outward action, and supports this with two Prophetic proofs. This lesson clarifies a common confusion and gives you a precise understanding of how these concepts coexist.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once without analysis, then the English translation. Absorb the author's argument as a whole before dissecting.
2
Identify the definition of tawakkul
Find where the author defines tawakkul. Notice that it is described as a quality of the heart (sifat al-qalb) and includes reliance, fear, hope, and viewing provision from Allah.
Highlight the phrase 'التوكل من صفة القلب'.
3
Analyze the two proofs
The author provides a hadith about seeking lawful wealth and a report of the Prophet's own practice. Consider how each proof demonstrates that outward effort does not undermine tawakkul.
The first proof contrasts intentions; the second shows that the Prophet himself stored provisions.
4
Reflect on the core distinction
Ask yourself: Why does the author emphasize that viewing provision as from acquisition is disbelief? How does this reinforce the inner nature of tawakkul?
This distinction is key to understanding the compatibility of kasb and tawakkul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا أنا نقول: التوكل على الله فريضةٌ. والاكتساب لا يرفض التوكل، لأن التوكل من صفة القلب وهو الثقة بالله تعالى، والخوف والرجاء من الله تعالى، ورؤية الرزق من الله تعالى؛ لأن رؤية الرزق من الكَسْبِ كفر وضلال، ومن الله دِينُ وشَرِيعة. يدل عليه ما روي عن النبي لا اله إلا أنه قال : من طلب الدنيا حلالا استعفافًا عن المسألة وسعيًا على عياله وتعطفًا على جاره، جاء يوم القيامة وجهه كالقمر ليلة البدر، ومن طلب الدنيا حلالا مفاخرًا مكاثرًا لقي الله تعالى يوم القيامة وهو عليه غضبان. يدل عليه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يدَّخر لنسائه قوت سنة.
But we say: Trust in God is an obligation. And acquisition does not negate trust in God, because trust in God is a quality of the heart, and it is reliance upon God Almighty, and fear and hope from God Almighty, and viewing provision as from God Almighty; because viewing provision as from acquisition is disbelief and misguidance, and [viewing it] from God is religion and law. Evidence for this is what is narrated from the Prophet (may there be no god but He) that he said: 'Whoever seeks the world lawfully, seeking chastity from begging, and striving for his dependents, and showing kindness to his neighbor, will come on the Day of Resurrection with his face like the full moon on the night of the full moon; and whoever seeks the world lawfully out of pride and boasting will meet God Almighty on the Day of Resurrection while He is angry with him.' Evidence for this is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to store for his wives a year's worth of sustenance.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the Sunni refutation against the claim that kasb (acquisition) is forbidden because it contradicts tawakkul (trust in God). The author states: 'But we say: Trust in God is an obligation. And acquisition does not negate trust in God.' He then defines tawakkul as a quality of the heart (sifat al-qalb), consisting of three elements: reliance (thiqah) upon God, fear (khawf) and hope (raja') from God, and viewing provision (riza) as from God alone. The author emphasizes that considering provision to come from one's own acquisition (kasb) is kufr (disbelief) and dhalal (misguidance), whereas considering it from God is true religion and shari'a. This distinction clarifies that tawakkul is an inner state, not negated by the outward action of seeking livelihood. The author then provides two prophetic proofs. First, a hadith about seeking lawful worldly wealth: if done with the intention of avoiding begging, supporting one's family, and being kind to neighbors, the person will shine like the full moon on Judgment Day; but if done out of pride and boasting, it earns God's anger. This shows that kasb with a good intention is virtuous and not opposed to tawakkul. Second, the author cites the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who used to store enough food for his wives for a year, demonstrating that saving for the future is not incompatible with tawakkul. Thus, the refutation is grounded in both conceptual clarification and textual evidence.

Key Terms

صفة القلب
الثقة
الخوف
الرجاء
رؤية الرزق
الكسب
كفر
ضلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that true tawakkul requires abandoning all worldly effort and livelihood.
Correction: The passage clarifies that tawakkul is an inner state of reliance on God, not the absence of action. Lawful acquisition with a good heart is compatible and even commendable.

Checkpoint
How does the author define tawakkul in this passage?
A) Abandoning all worldly work and relying solely on prayer
B) A quality of the heart that includes reliance on God, fear, hope, and seeing provision from God
C) A physical act of worship performed at specific times
D) Hoarding wealth for future security

Key Takeaway
Trust in God (tawakkul) is a quality of the heart that does not conflict with seeking lawful provision; the key is one's intention and inner reliance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan for your future—saving money, investing, or even just buying groceries for the week—do you ever feel a tension between that planning and your trust in Allah? How does the Prophet's example of storing food for a year challenge or affirm your current practice? Will you consciously align your heart to see that provision as from Allah, even as you act?
?
Think of a time you worked very hard for a result, and it came. To whom did you mentally attribute that success—your own effort or Allah's provision? If viewing provision as from kasb is disbelief (kufr), what might that say about your hidden assumptions? What concrete step can you take today to remind yourself that every provision is from Allah, not from your skill?
?

Honestly, which intention drives most of your daily work? If you find pride or show-off creeping in, what will you do to purify your intention before your next task?

God's Ongoing Creation: Refuting the Claim of Finality
Nasafi refutes the claim of finality in creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's creation is ongoing and continuous, refuting the claim that He finished creating after the initial act.

Core Idea
God's creative power is not a one-time event; He creates new things every day.

This lesson tackles a fundamental misunderstanding about divine power. Some claimed that God created everything at once and then stopped. Nasafi refutes this by presenting the Sunni position that God decreed all things but creates them at their appointed times, supported by Quranic verses and prophetic teachings. Prepare to see how God's continuous creation is woven into the fabric of existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation once to get the flow of the argument. Notice the two opposing views.
2
Identify the false claim
Find the statement of 'some people of falsehood'. What do they believe about creation? Note their proof from the Quran.
3
Understand the Sunni response
Read the Sunni position: God decreed all things but creates them later. How does this differ from the false claim?
4
Examine the evidence
Look at the Quranic verse 'Every day He is in a new affair' and its interpretations by the Prophet and Ali. What do they teach about God's ongoing activity?
5
Reflect on implications
Think about why this matters for tawhid. Does God's continuous creation diminish His power or magnify it?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على المفروغية القائلين إن الله خلق كل الأشياء ولم يبق شيء لم يخلقه قال بعض أهل الباطل : إن الله تعالى خلق الأشياء كلها ولم يبق شيء غير مخلوق حتى يخلقه الآن، وكل ما كان مخلوقاً فرغ منها، حتى إن الثمار في الأشجار كلها، إلا أنها غير ظاهرة ونحن لا نراها وهي في الحقيقة مخلوقة. واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ لَكُم مَّا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٩]. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : إن الله تعالى قدر ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة، ولم يخلقها حين قدرها، وإنما يخلقها بعد ذلك في كل وقت وأوان، خلق ما مضى وفي المستقبل يخلقها. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: كُلَّ يَوْمٍ هُوَ فِي شَأْنٍ ﴾ [الرحمن: ۲۹] قال عليه السلام: «شأنه أن يحيي ويميت ويُعزّ ويُذل . وعن علي رضي الله عنه : أنه سُئل عن قوله تعالى: كُلَّ يَوْمٍ هُوَ فِي شَأْنٍ ﴾ [الرحمن: ٢٩] فقال: «شأنه أن يسوق النطفة من أصلاب الآباء إلى أرحام الأمهات، ثم يصور صورة ثم يُخرج من بطن الأم إلي الدنيا، ثم يميته، ثم يحييه يوم القيامة».
Chapter on refuting the proponents of finality who say that God created all things and nothing remains that He did not create. Some people of falsehood said: God created all things and nothing remains uncreated for Him to create now, and everything that was created He has finished from it, even the fruits on the trees are all [created], except they are not apparent and we do not see them, but in reality they are created. And they argued with His saying: 'He it is Who created for you all that is on the earth' [Al-Baqara 2:29]. Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a said: God decreed what will happen until the Day of Resurrection, and He did not create them when He decreed them; rather He creates them after that in every time and season. He created what has passed, and in the future He creates them. This is supported by His saying: 'Every day He is in a new affair' [Al-Rahman 55:29]. He ﷺ said: 'His affair is that He gives life and causes death, and exalts and abases.' And from Ali رضي الله عنه: He was asked about His saying: 'Every day He is in a new affair' [Al-Rahman 55:29] and he said: 'His affair is that He drives the drop from the loins of fathers to the wombs of mothers, then He forms a form, then He brings it out from the mother's womb into the world, then He causes it to die, then He revives it on the Day of Resurrection.'
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that God created everything at once and has finished creating. The opponents (some people of falsehood) argue that everything is already created, even fruits on trees though not yet visible, and they cite the Quranic verse 'He it is Who created for you all that is on the earth.' The Sunni response is that God decreed (qaddara) everything that will happen until the Day of Resurrection, but He did not create them at the time of decree; rather, He creates them later at each time and season. They support this with the verse 'Every day He is in a new affair' and the Prophet's explanation that His affairs include giving life, causing death, exalting, and abasing. Ali ibn Abi Talib further explains this verse as referring to God's continuous creative act in the process of human generation: moving the drop from loins to wombs, forming it, bringing it out, causing death, and resurrecting on Judgment Day. This demonstrates that creation is ongoing, not a one-time event.

Key Terms
المفروغية
قدر
خلق
كل يوم هو في شأن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power is only expressed in initial creation, and He does not create anything new after that.
Correction: This passage shows that God continuously creates new things every day, as indicated by the verse 'Every day He is in a new affair' and the examples given.

Checkpoint
What do the Sunni theologians (Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a) affirm regarding God's creation?
A) God created everything at once and then stopped.
B) God decreed all things but creates them only when they occur.
C) God creates nothing new after the initial creation.
D) Only the resurrection is a new creation.

Key Takeaway
God's creation is not a single past event; He continuously creates new things each day, as demonstrated by the Quran and Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you wake up tomorrow, will you truly believe that God is creating new things in your life—your breath, your thoughts, the events of the day—or do you live as if everything is already fixed and finished? Write down one way you will consciously depend on His continuous creation today.
?
The Prophet explained 'every day He is in a new affair' as giving life, causing death, exalting, and abasing. Which of these four realities are you trying to ignore? Where in your life are you resisting God's current 'affair'—perhaps in a situation where you need to be humbled or where you need to let go of control? Commit to surrendering that area today.

The Uncreated Decree and the Command to the Pen
Proof that the decree is uncreated, with objection and answer about the Pen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the divine decree (qadar) is considered uncreated according to Ahl al-Sunnah, and how the Pen's command supports this without implying creation of the decree.

Core Idea
The decree is uncreated; the Pen is created but merely writes what God already knows.

This passage presents a key argument in kalam about the nature of the divine decree. The author begins by stating that God's decree concerning the Day of Resurrection is not created, then provides a proof from the command to the Pen. Objections about the Pen's life and the wisdom of the command are answered, reinforcing that the decree itself is uncreated and that God alone knows the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a claim, a proof, then two objections with responses.
The passage uses a concise argumentative style common in kalam texts.
2
Understand the main proof
The author argues that if the decree were created, we would already be in the Resurrection. Then he gives the proof from the Pen: God created the Pen and commanded it to write all that happens until the Day of Resurrection.
This shows the decree is recorded but not created as a thing.
3
Analyze the objections and answers
The first objection asks about the Pen's life; the answer says it is inanimate but made to speak. The second objection questions the wisdom of commanding the Pen when God knows all; the answer is to demonstrate God's exclusive knowledge of the unseen.
These answers refute misunderstandings about the createdness of the decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يدل عليه أن الله تعالى قدر يوم القيامة وليس بمخلوق؛ ولأنه لو كان مخلوقاً لكنا نحن في القيامة وليس كذلك. ويدل عليه : أن الله تعالى خلق القلم ، وقال : اكتب ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة. فإن قيل : القلم هل فيه حياة؟ قلنا ليس فيه حياة، لكنه جمادٌ يستنطقه الله كما يستنطق الأحياء. فإن قيل: أيش الحكمة في أنَّ الله تعالى أمر القلم بأن يكتب على اللوح المحفوظ ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة وهو عالم؟ قلنا : لكي يُعلم أن الله تعالى يعلم الغيب ولا يعلم الغيب إلا الله.
This indicates that God Almighty has decreed the Day of Resurrection and it is not created; because if it were created, we would be in the Resurrection and that is not the case. And it is indicated by the fact that God Almighty created the Pen and said: Write what will be until the Day of Resurrection. If it is said: Does the Pen have life? We say: It has no life, but it is an inanimate object that God causes to speak just as He causes living beings to speak. If it is said: What is the wisdom in God Almighty commanding the Pen to write on the Preserved Tablet what will be until the Day of Resurrection, while He is All-Knowing? We say: So that it be known that God Almighty knows the unseen and none knows the unseen except God.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that the divine decree (qadar) concerning the Day of Resurrection is not created. The author first states that God's decree is uncreated, arguing that if it were created, then we would be created in the Resurrection—which is not the case. Then a second proof is given: God created the Pen and commanded it to write all that will happen until the Day of Resurrection. An objection arises: Does the Pen have life to obey? The answer: It has no life; it is an inanimate object that God causes to speak, just as He makes living beings speak. Another objection asks: What is the wisdom of commanding the Pen to write since God already knows all? The answer: So that it becomes known that God alone knows the unseen, and no one else. Throughout, the author maintains that the decree itself is uncreated, as it is an attribute of God's knowledge.

Key Terms
القلم (al-qalam)
قدر (qadar)
اللوح المحفوظ (al-lawh al-mahfuz)
القيامة (al-qiyama)
جماد (jamad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since the Pen is created, the decree (what it writes) is also created.
Correction: The decree is uncreated; the Pen is a created instrument that records what God already knows.

Checkpoint
Why does the author state that the decree (qadar) of the Day of Resurrection is not created?
A) Because the Pen is created and writes it.
B) Because if it were created, we would be in the Resurrection now.
C) Because God commanded the Pen to write it.
D) Because it is on the Preserved Tablet.

Key Takeaway
The divine decree is uncreated because it is an attribute of God's knowledge, and the Pen merely records what is already determined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every event in your life—every joy and every trial—has been decreed by God from eternity, and that this decree is uncreated? How does this belief affect your patience in hardship and your gratitude in ease? Will you commit to reminding yourself of this when you face something you did not plan?
?
God commanded the Pen to write to show that He alone knows the unseen. Are you living as if the future is in your hands, or do you genuinely entrust it to the One who knows all? What is one worry about tomorrow that you need to surrender to Him today?
?
The Pen is inanimate yet obeyed God's command. When God commands you through His revelation, do you obey immediately like the Pen, or do you hesitate and rationalize? What is one command from Allah that you have been delaying, and when will you act on it?

The Eternity of Paradise and Hell: Refuting the Annihilation Claim
Nasafi refutes the Jahmiyya claim, affirming the eternity of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna arguments for the eternal duration of Paradise and Hell, and how they refute the Jahmiyya claim of annihilation.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are eternal because God's justice prevents Him from revoking His reward and punishment.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents the Sunni position on the eternity of Paradise and Hell. He counters the Jahmiyya claim that both will be annihilated, using Quranic evidence, rational analogy, and a reinterpretation of problematic narrations. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the compact style typical of classical kalam works.
2
Identify the main principle
The passage opens with the creedal statement: Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes for reward and punishment. Why does this lead to the conclusion that they will not be annihilated?
The key is that annihilation would contradict their purpose.
3
Examine the Quranic proof and analogy
Nasafi cites Surah at-Tawba 9:111 and interprets it as a transaction. Believers purchase Paradise with faith, deeds, and intentions. The analogy from human commerce shows that a seller cannot revoke a sale after receiving payment, else it would be unjust.
This analogy relies on the principle that God does not commit injustice.
4
Understand the responses to objections
Nasafi addresses two objections: (1) the verse 'He is the First and the Last' (al-Hadid 3) — he explains that God's eternity is self-subsistent while creation's eternity is by God's preservation; (2) the report about Hell becoming empty — he interprets it as a temporary state after the sinful believers leave, not annihilation.
These responses show how Sunni scholars harmonize texts that apparently contradict each other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: الجنة والنار دارا الخلد، وهما للثواب والعقاب فلا يفنيان على ما ذكرنا، ولأنه لا يجوز منه الظلم والجور. قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ اشْتَرَى مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَنفُسَهُمْ وَأَمْوَالَهُم بِأَنَّ لَهُمُ الْجَنَّةَ ﴾ [التوبة: ١١١] اشترى أهل الجنة الجنة بإيمانهم، والدرجات بأعمالهم، والرؤية بنياتهم. والكفار اشتروا النار بنياتهم وكفرهم، ورأينا أنَّ مَنْ اسْتَرى دارًا وسلَّم الثَّمَنَ لا يحسن من البائع أن يستردها منه، فإن فعل ذلك يكون منه ظلما وجورا، والله سبحانه وتعالى منزه عن الظلم والجور. وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ وَالْآخِرُ وَالظَّهِرُ وَالْبَاطِنُ ﴾ [الحديد: ٣]. قلنا: نعم، ولكن هو باق لا بإبقاء أحد، والخلق باق بإبقاء الله تعالى، فظهرت التفرقة بين الخالق والمخلوق. وأما معنى الخبر : قلنا: إذا خرج العُصَاةُ من النار وذهبوا إلى الجنة تبقي النار صحراء ليس فيها أحدٌ، وهذا هو معنى الخبر.
And the People of the Sunna and the Community said: Paradise and Hell are the abodes of eternity, and they are for reward and punishment, so they will not be annihilated, as we have mentioned, and because injustice and tyranny are not permissible from Him. Allah Most High said: 'Indeed, Allah has purchased from the believers their lives and their properties [in exchange] for that they will have Paradise' (at-Tawba 111). The people of Paradise purchased Paradise with their faith, and degrees with their deeds, and the vision (of Allah) with their intentions. And the disbelievers purchased Hell with their intentions and disbelief. And we see that whoever buys a house and pays the price, it is not good for the seller to take it back from him; if he does that, it would be injustice and tyranny from him, and Allah is exalted above injustice and tyranny. As for His saying, 'He is the First and the Last, the Manifest and the Hidden': we say: Yes, but He is eternal without anyone preserving Him, while creation is eternal by Allah's preservation, so the distinction between Creator and creature became apparent. As for the meaning of the report: we say: When the disobedient come out of Hell and go to Paradise, Hell remains an empty desert with no one in it, and that is the meaning of the report.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents the Ahl al-Sunna refutation of the Jahmiyya claim. First, they assert the basic principle: Paradise and Hell are eternal abodes created for reward and punishment; they will never be annihilated because annihilation would entail injustice on God's part, which is impossible. The author then supports this with the Quranic verse from Surat at-Tawba (9:111). This verse is interpreted as a transaction: believers purchased Paradise by giving their lives and property; similarly, the disbelievers purchased Hell with their intentions and disbelief. Using an analogy from human commerce, if a seller takes back a house after receiving the price, that would be unjust. Since God is just, He will not revoke the transaction. Next, the author addresses the proof verse (al-Hadid 3) used by the Jahmiyya. He concedes that God is eternal without need of preservation, but created things exist only by God's preservation. Thus the verse does not imply the annihilation of Paradise and Hell; rather, it distinguishes between God's self-subsistence and the contingent existence of creatures. Finally, the author interprets the hadith about Hell's doors: it refers only to the temporary state after the sinful believers are removed from Hell (after purification) and go to Paradise, leaving Hell empty of them. It does not mean annihilation of Hell itself. Thus the Jahmiyya misinterpretation is resolved.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
دار الخلد
الظلم والجور
الاشتراء
التفرقة بين الخالق والمخلوق
معنى الخبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about Hell's doors blowing with wind proves that Hell will be completely annihilated.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna interpret this hadith as referring to a temporary state after the sinful believers leave Hell for Paradise; Hell remains but is empty of inhabitants.

Checkpoint
How does Ahl al-Sunna interpret the hadith about a day when Hell's doors blow with wind?
A) It means Hell will be completely annihilated
B) It refers to a time after the sinful believers leave Hell for Paradise
C) It is a weak hadith and thus rejected
D) It refers to a future event after the Day of Judgment when Hell is destroyed

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are eternal; God's justice and the Quranic transaction analogy confirm that they will never be annihilated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that Paradise and Hell are eternal. But do you live today as if your actions are literally buying an eternal home? What transaction are you making with your time, wealth, and intentions right now? Write down one concrete change you will make today to 'pay the price' for Paradise.
?
The analogy of the seller taking back a house is used to show God's justice. If God were unjust, He could take back His promise. But He is just. Are you relying on God's justice as a guarantee of salvation, or are you using it as a safety net for sin? What would it mean for you to truly believe that God will never revoke His transaction with believers—even if you fall short?
?
Nasafi distinguishes between God's self-subsistence and creation's preservation. You know that everything depends on God for existence. How does this make you feel about your own dependency? Can you genuinely accept that you exist only by God's preservation every second? What would change in your day if you truly felt that?

Pleasure and Anger as Eternal Attributes of Allah
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila denial of pleasure and anger as divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna affirm that pleasure and anger are real eternal attributes of Allah, and how the Quran distinguishes them from created rewards and punishments.

Core Idea
Pleasure and anger are real, eternal attributes of Allah, not just metaphors for reward and punishment.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi tackles a key debate between the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna over divine attributes. The Mu'tazila claimed that 'pleasure' and 'anger' in the Quran refer only to Paradise and Hell, denying they are real attributes. Ahl al-Sunna, however, affirm them as eternal attributes without modality. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila position
Read the first part of the passage where the Mu'tazila argue that pleasure and anger cannot be attributes because Allah does not change, and that these terms in the Quran mean Paradise and Hell.
Notice their reasoning is based on the impossibility of change in Allah.
2
Learn the Ahl al-Sunna affirmation
Read the Ahl al-Sunna response: pleasure and anger are eternal attributes like will, hearing, sight, and speech, without modality or anthropomorphism.
They do not involve change, so they are compatible with Allah's perfection.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Look at the four Quranic verses cited. Observe how each verse mentions Paradise or Hell alongside pleasure or anger as distinct entities, proving they are separate attributes.
Focus on verse 9:72 where 'pleasure from Allah is greater' shows pleasure is an additional attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكلام على القائلين بأن الرضا والسخط ليسا من صفات الله تعالى. قالت المعتزلة : الرّضا والسَّخَط ليسا من صفات الله تعالى؛ لأن الله تعالى لا تتغير عليه الأحوال، وكل موضع ذَكَرَ الرضا والسخط أراد به الجنة والنار. وقال أهل السنة الرضا والسَّخَط من صفات الله أزلية بلا كيف وتشبيه، ولا يتغير من حال إلى حال، كسائر الصفات مثل الإرادة والسمع والبصر والكلام. فالدليل على أن الرضا غير الجنة قوله تعالى: ﴿جَزَاؤُهُمْ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ جَنَّتُ عَدْنٍ تَجْرِى من تحبها الأَنهرُ خَلِدِينَ فِيهَا أَبَدًا رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ وَرَضُوا عَنْهُ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ خَشِيَ رَبَّهُ ﴾ [البينة: ۸] وكذلك قوله تعالى ﴿يُبَشِّرُهُمْ رَبُّهُم بِرَحْمَةٍ مِّنْهُ وَرِضْوَانٍ وَجَنَّتٍ لَّهُمْ فِيهَانَعِيمٌ مُّقِيمُ ﴾ [التوبة: ٢١] وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَسَكِنَ طَيِّبَةً فِي جَنَّتِ عَدْنٍ وَرِضْوَانٌ مِّنَ اللَّهِ أكْبَرُ ذَلِكَ هُوَ الْفَوْزُ الْعَظِيمُ ﴾ [التوبة: ۷۲] وكذلك في طرف الشخط قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَلِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ ولَعَنَهُ وَأَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا ﴾ [النساء: ۹۳] فَصَلَ بين الرضا والجنة، والنار والسخط.
Chapter: On the discussion regarding those who say that pleasure (ar-riḍā) and anger (as-sakhaṭ) are not among the attributes of Allah. The Muʿtazila said: Pleasure and anger are not among the attributes of Allah, because Allah is not subject to changing states. And every place where He mentioned pleasure and anger, He intended by them Paradise and the Fire. And the Ahl al-Sunna said: Pleasure and anger are among the attributes of Allah, eternal (azaliyya), without modality (kayf) and without anthropomorphism (tashbīh), and they do not change from one state to another, just like other attributes such as will (al-irāda), hearing (as-samʿ), sight (al-baṣar), and speech (al-kalām). The evidence that pleasure is other than Paradise is His saying: 'Their reward with their Lord is Gardens of Eden, beneath which rivers flow, abiding therein forever; Allah is pleased with them and they are pleased with Him. That is for those who fear their Lord.' [Al-Bayyinah 8]. And likewise His saying: 'Their Lord gives them good news of mercy from Him and pleasure and Gardens for them wherein is enduring bliss.' [At-Tawbah 21]. And likewise His saying: 'And pleasant dwellings in Gardens of Eden; and pleasure from Allah is greater. That is the great triumph.' [At-Tawbah 72]. And likewise regarding the opposite, anger, His saying: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his reward is Hell, abiding therein forever, and Allah is angry with him and has cursed him and prepared for him a great punishment.' [An-Nisā' 93]. So He made a distinction between pleasure and Paradise, and between the Fire and anger.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a doctrinal debate on whether pleasure (riḍā) and anger (sakhaṭ) are real attributes of Allah. The Muʿtazila deny them, arguing that Allah does not change (lā tataġayyaru ʿalayhi al-aḥwāl), so these terms in the Quran refer only to created rewards and punishments (Paradise and Hell). In response, Ahl al-Sunna affirm that pleasure and anger are eternal (azaliyya) attributes, without modality (kayf) or anthropomorphism (tashbīh), and they do not change. The proof is scriptural: verses like Al-Bayyinah 8, At-Tawbah 21, and At-Tawbah 72 mention Paradise and Allah's pleasure as distinct entities, the latter being greater. Similarly, An-Nisā' 93 mentions Hell and Allah's anger separately. Thus, the Quran itself distinguishes between the reward and the attribute, confirming that pleasure and anger are real, eternal attributes.

معتزلة

Misconception: Pleasure and anger are merely metaphorical expressions for reward and punishment, not real attributes.
Correction: The Quran distinguishes between pleasure/anger and Paradise/Hell, showing they are real, eternal attributes of Allah.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself distinguishes between pleasure/anger and Paradise/Hell, confirming that these are real eternal attributes of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila rejected Allah's anger because it seemed to imply change. Are there any of Allah's attributes that you struggle to accept simply because they challenge your intellect? How does this lesson call you to submit to revelation over human reasoning?

The Divine Attributes of Pleasure and Wrath
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila denial and Sunni affirmation of rida and sakhat as eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila denial of pleasure and wrath as attributes of Allah, the Sunni affirmation of them as eternal attributes without modality, and the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Pleasure and wrath are real, eternal attributes of Allah, not metaphors for reward and punishment.

This lesson presents a foundational debate in Islamic theology: are pleasure (rida) and wrath (sakhat) real attributes of God? The Mu'tazila denied them and interpreted scriptural references as Paradise and Hellfire. The Ahl al-Sunna affirmed them as eternal, unchangeable attributes, similar to will, hearing, sight, and speech. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Sunni commitment to affirming all divine attributes without anthropomorphism or change.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its literal translation to grasp both positions clearly without interpretation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila argument
Note their reasoning: God's states do not change, so pleasure and wrath cannot be attributes; wherever mentioned, they refer to Paradise and Hellfire.
The Mu'tazila reject anthropomorphic implications.
3
Contrast with the Sunni position
The Sunni school affirms rida and sakhat as eternal attributes without how (bila kayf) and without anthropomorphism (bila tashbih), and they do not change.
This aligns with other attributes like will, hearing, sight, and speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكلام على القائلين بأن الرضا والسخط ليسا من صفات الله تعالى قالت المعتزلة : الرّضا والسَّخَط ليسا من صفات الله تعالى؛ لأن الله تعالى لا تتغير عليه الأحوال، وكل موضع ذَكَرَ [فيه] الرضا والسخط أراد به الجنة والنار. وقال أهل السنة الرضا والسَّخَط من صفات الله أزلية بلا كيف وتشبيه، ولا يتغير من حال إلى حال، كسائر الصفات مثل الإرادة والسمع والبصر والكلام.
Section on discoursing with those who say that pleasure and wrath are not from the attributes of God. The Mu'tazila said: Pleasure and wrath are not from the attributes of God, because God's states do not change, and wherever He mentioned [in it] pleasure and wrath He meant Paradise and Hellfire. The Ahl al-Sunna said: Pleasure and wrath are from the attributes of God, eternal without how and without anthropomorphism, and they do not change from state to state, like the rest of the attributes such as will, hearing, sight, and speech.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents the opposing positions of the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna regarding the divine attributes of pleasure (rida) and wrath (sakhat). The Mu'tazila deny that these are real attributes of God, arguing that God's states do not change, and interpret scriptural mentions of pleasure and wrath as referring to Paradise and Hellfire respectively. The Ahl al-Sunna affirm that rida and sakhat are eternal attributes of God, without modality or anthropomorphism. They do not change, just like other attributes such as will, hearing, sight, and speech. This establishes the Sunni doctrine that these attributes are real, eternal, and not subject to change.

Correction: Sunni theologians affirm these attributes as eternal and unchanging, without anthropomorphism.

Qur'anic Proofs Distinguishing Pleasure from Paradise
Nasafi provides four Qur'anic verses to prove the distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Qur'anic verses to demonstrate that divine pleasure and wrath are distinct from Paradise and Hellfire.

Core Idea
The Qur'an separates divine pleasure from Paradise and wrath from Hell.

Nasafi now turns to scripture to fortify the rational distinction between divine attributes and their associated rewards. By citing explicit verses, he shows that pleasure (rida) and wrath (sakhat) are not mere metaphors but separate realities mentioned alongside Paradise and Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once to get the rhythm, then read the English translation. Notice the four verses cited.
The passage uses 'فالدليل على أن الرضا غير الجنة' as its thesis.
2
Identify the three proofs for pleasure
The first three verses all mention Paradise and pleasure together as separate blessings. List each one and note how they are distinct.
Surah al-Bayyinah (98:8), Surah al-Tawba (9:21), Surah al-Tawba (9:72).
3
Identify the proof for wrath
The fourth verse (Surah al-Nisa 4:93) mentions Hell and Allah's wrath together but as distinct punishments.
The verse uses 'وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ' alongside 'جَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ'.
4
Understand the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that the Qur'an separates pleasure from Paradise and wrath from Hell, proving they are distinct realities.

فالدليل على أن الرضا غير الجنة قوله تعالى: {جَزَاؤُهُمْ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ جَنَّتُ عَدْنٍ تَجْرِي مِن تَحْتِهَا الْأَنْهَارُ خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا أَبَدًا رَّضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ وَرَضُوا عَنْهُ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ خَشِيَ رَبَّهُ} وكذلك قوله تعالى {يُبَشِّرُهُمْ رَبُّهُم بِرَحْمَةٍ مِّنْهُ وَرِضْوَانٍ وَجَنَّاتٍ لَّهُمْ فِيهَا نَعِيمٌ مُّقِيمٌ} وكذلك قوله تعالى {وَمَسَاكِنَ طَيِّبَةً فِي جَنَّاتِ عَدْنٍ وَرِضْوَانٌ مِّنَ اللَّهِ أَكْبَرُ ذَلِكَ هُوَ الْفَوْزُ الْعَظِيمُ} وكذلك في طرف السخط قوله تعالى: {وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا وَغَضِبَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَعَنَهُ وَأَعَدَّ لَهُ عَذَابًا عَظِيمًا} فَصَلَ بَيْنَ الرِّضَا وَالْجَنَّةِ، وَالنَّارِ وَالسَّخَطِ.
The proof that pleasure is other than Paradise is His statement: 'Their reward is with their Lord: Gardens of Eden, under which rivers flow, abiding therein forever. Allah is pleased with them and they are pleased with Him. That is for him who fears his Lord.' And likewise His statement: 'Their Lord gives them good tidings of mercy from Him and pleasure and gardens for them wherein is enduring bliss.' And likewise His statement: 'And pleasant dwellings in Gardens of Eden. And pleasure from Allah is greater. That is the great attainment.' And likewise with regard to wrath, His statement: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and Allah has become angry with him and has cursed him and has prepared for him a great punishment.' So He separated between pleasure and Paradise, and between Hellfire and wrath.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage provides the proof that divine pleasure (rida) is not the same as Paradise (janna), and divine wrath (sakhat) is not the same as Hellfire (nar). The author cites four verses: from Surah al-Bayyinah (98:8) where Allah mentions His pleasure alongside Paradise as a reward, indicating they are distinct. Then from Surah al-Tawba (9:21) where mercy, pleasure, and gardens are listed separately. Then from Surah al-Tawba (9:72) where pleasure from Allah is described as greater than gardens. Then from Surah al-Nisa (4:93) regarding the one who kills a believer, where Allah's wrath is mentioned alongside Hell, showing wrath is separate. The conclusion: the Qur'an clearly separates these concepts, proving they are distinct realities.

Misconception: Some think that divine pleasure is merely a metaphor for Paradise or that wrath is just a description of Hellfire.
Correction: These verses explicitly list pleasure alongside Paradise as a separate reward, and wrath alongside Hell as a separate punishment, proving they are distinct realities.

Key Takeaway

Why God's Attributes Cannot Change
Nasafi records a question about change in God's attributes and the answer explaining its impossibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the question of change in God's attributes is considered impossible in Islamic theology, based on the reasoning of Nasr ibn Darir.

Core Idea
Change in God's attributes would imply they are created, contradicting their eternity.

This lesson presents a short question-and-answer exchange from Imam Nasafi's Bahr al-Kalam. The scholar Nasr ibn Darir al-Khatli is asked whether God's attributes can change. His answer cuts directly to the impossibility of such a change, grounding it in the oneness and eternity of God's attributes. He then illustrates his reasoning with an analogy about creating a being like God.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that the question is answered immediately with 'impossible' (muhal).
2
Follow the logical argument
Identify the core reasoning: God is one and eternal with all His attributes. Change would make an attribute created, but God's attributes are uncreated.
This is the key premise that leads to the impossibility.
3
Consider the analogy
Examine the analogy about creating the like of God. Understanding this parallel will deepen your grasp of the argument against change in attributes.
The analogy reinforces that nothing is like God, so His attributes cannot become like created things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَسُئِلَ الشَّيْخُ الْمُفَسِّرُ نَصْرُ بْنُ ضَرِيرٍ الْخَتْلِيُّ : إِنَّ الله تَعَالَى هَلْ تَتَغَيَّرُ صِفَاتُهُ؟ فَأَجَابَ وَقَالَ: هَذَا السُّؤَالُ مُحَالٌ، لِأَنَّ الله تَعَالَى بِجَمِيعِ صِفَاتِهِ وَاحِدٌ، وَبِجَمِيعِ صِفَاتِهِ قَدِيمٌ، فَلَوْ غُيِّرَ شَيْءٌ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ تَكُونُ تِلْكَ الصِّفَةُ مُحْدَثَةً مَخْلُوقَةً، وَصِفَاتُ الله غَيْرُ مَخْلُوقَةٍ، وَهَذَا كَمَا يُسْأَلُونَ أَنَّ الله تَعَالَى هَلْ يَقْدِرُ عَلَى أَنْ يَخْلُقَ مِثْلَهُ؟ فَالْجَوَابُ عَنْ هَذَا: أَنَّ السُّؤَالَ مُحَالٌ؛ لِأَنَّ الله تَعَالَى قَدِيمٌ، فَلَوْ خَلَقَ شَيْئًا يَكُونُ ذَلِكَ الْمَخْلُوقَ فَكَيْفَ يَكُونُ مِثْلَهُ وَالله تَعَالَى مَا خَلَقَ شَيْئاً فِي الْأَزَلِ، فَوَجَبَ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ غَيْرُهُ مِثْلَهُ.
The interpreting scholar Nasr ibn Darir al-Khatli was asked: Does God's attributes change? He answered and said: This question is impossible, because God is one with all His attributes, and eternal with all His attributes. So if anything of His attributes were changed, that attribute would be originated and created, but God's attributes are uncreated. This is like when they ask: Is God able to create the like of Himself? The answer to this is that the question is impossible; because God is eternal, so if He created something, that thing would be created, so how could it be like Him, and God did not create anything in pre-eternity. So it is necessary that nothing other than Him is like Him.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage records a question posed to the scholar Nasr ibn Darir al-Khatli about whether God's attributes can change. The answer begins by declaring the question impossible (muhāl). The reasoning: God, with all His attributes, is one and eternal. If any attribute changed, it would become originated and created, but God's attributes are uncreated. Then an analogy is given: it is like asking whether God can create a being like Himself. That question is also impossible because God is eternal, and anything He creates would be created and temporal, thus cannot be like the eternal. The conclusion: no other being can be like God, and similarly, His attributes do not change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that attributing actions like being pleased or angry to God implies change in His attributes.
Correction: This answer clarifies that such questions are based on a false analogy. God's attributes are eternal and uncreated; any appearance of change in divine actions relates to temporal effects, not to change in the attributes themselves.

D) Because attributes are not real

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are eternal and uncreated; therefore, any suggestion of change is impossible.

The Impossibility of Change in God's Attributes
Nasafi answers whether God's attributes can change, deeming the question impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is impossible for God's attributes to change, and why the question itself is considered invalid in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Change in God's attributes would make them created, contradicting His eternity.

This passage presents a direct question about the possibility of change in God's attributes, along with the scholar's answer. It establishes a key principle: God is eternal with all His attributes, so any change would imply temporality. The reasoning is then reinforced with a parallel argument about God creating a being like Himself. Let's read the source passage and unpack its logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the question-and-answer format.
The scholar begins by stating the question before refuting it.
2
Identify the main argument
The answer declares the question impossible. Why? Because God is one and eternal with all His attributes. Change would make an attribute created.
3
Recognize the parallel argument
The scholar then gives a similar example: asking if God can create a being like Himself. This is also impossible because God is eternal and any created thing is contingent.
Both arguments rely on God's eternity.
4
Reflect on the principle
Both arguments rest on the same principle: God's eternity and uniqueness preclude any change or likeness.
This is a foundational concept in divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So he answered and said: 'This question is impossible, because God Most High is one with all His attributes, and eternal with all His attributes. So it is necessary that nothing other than Him is like Him.'

Commentary
This passage refutes the question of whether God's attributes can change. It begins by stating the question: can God's attributes change? The answer declares the question inherently impossible (muhal). The reasoning is that God is one and eternal with all His attributes. Change would imply that an attribute becomes originated (hadith) and created, but God's attributes are uncreated. Then a parallel argument is given: the question of whether God can create a being like Himself is similarly impossible because God is eternal, and any created thing is contingent and cannot be like the eternal. The passage concludes that nothing other than God can be His equal.

God's Knowledge of the Unending Breaths of Paradise and Hell
Nasafi refutes Jahmiyya objection regarding God's knowledge of breaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Jahmiyya dilemma regarding God's knowledge of the breaths of the people of Paradise and Hell, and why the continued existence of created beings does not imply equality with God.

Core Idea
God knows every breath, but they are uncountable and unceasing.

The Jahmiyya posed a dilemma: either God does not know the number of breaths of the people of Paradise and Hell (implying ignorance) or He does know (implying those breaths are finite and thus the people perish). In this passage, Imam Nasafi provides a decisive refutation, clarifying the nature of God's knowledge and the contingency of created existence. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Jahmiyya dilemma
Read the passage carefully, noting the two horns of the dilemma: either God does not know (ignorance) or He knows (implying finitude and perishing).
The Jahmiyya assumed that knowledge entails finitude.
2
Nasafi's initial answer
Nasafi answers that God knows the breaths, but they are not countable and do not cease. This resolves the dilemma.
3
The equality objection
A further objection is raised: if the people of Paradise and Hell do not perish, they share everlastingness with God, implying equality.
4
The refutation
Nasafi explains that God's eternity is essential (without beginning or end), while the created's continuation is contingent upon God's preservation. Thus, no equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
وفي سؤال الجهمية : إنَّ الله تعالى هل يعلم عدد أنفاس أهل الجنة والنار أم لا؟ فإن قلت: لا، فقد وصفت الله تعالى بالجهل. وإن قلت : نعم، فقد قلت بأن أهل الجنة والنار يفنيان. والجواب عنه أن نقول: إن الله تعالى يعلم أن أنفاس أهل الجنة والنار وليست بمعدودة ولا تنقطع. فإن قيل: إذا قلتم بأنَّ أهل الجنة والنار لا يفنيان، فقد سوّيتم بينهم وبين الله تعالى. قلنا: لا يكون تسوية بينهم وبين الله تعالى، لأنَّ الله تعالى أوَّل قديم بلا ابتداء، وآخر حكيم بلا انتهاء، وأهل الجنة محدثون، وإنما يبقون ولا يفنون بإبقاء الله تعالى إيَّاهم، والله تعالى باقي لا بإبقاء أحد، فلا يكون تسوية بين الخالق والمخلوق.
Chapter. And from the question of the Jahmiyya: 'Does God Most High know the number of breaths of the people of Paradise and Hell or not? If you say: No, then you have described God Most High with ignorance. And if you say: Yes, then you have said that the people of Paradise and Hell perish.' The answer to it is that we say: 'God Most High knows that the breaths of the people of Paradise and Hell are uncountable and unceasing.' Then if it is said: 'If you say that the people of Paradise and Hell do not perish, then you have equated them with God Most High.' We say: 'There is no equality between them and God Most High, because God Most High is the First, Eternal without beginning, and the Last, Wise without end, while the people of Paradise are originated. They only remain and do not perish by God Most High's preservation of them, while God Most High remains not by anyone's preservation. So there is no equality between the Creator and the created.'
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage addresses a question from the Jahmiyya sect. They present a dilemma: either God does not know the number of breaths of the people of Paradise and Hell (which would imply ignorance) or He does know, which would imply that those people perish (because only a finite number of breaths can be known). The answer is that God knows their breaths, but they are not countable and do not cease. Then a further objection is raised: if the people of Paradise and Hell do not perish, they share everlastingness with God, implying equality. The refutation explains that the eternity of God is essential (eternal without beginning and without end) while the continued existence of the created is contingent upon God's preservation. Therefore, there is no equality.

Key Terms
الجهمية
أنفاس
المعدودة
الانقطاع
البقاء
الإبقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge of something finite implies that thing must come to an end.
Correction: God can know things that are unending; His knowledge does not impose finitude. The breaths of Paradise and Hell are unceasing, yet God knows them.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi answer the Jahmiyya objection that if God knows the breaths of Paradise and Hell, then those people must perish?
A) He says that God does not know the breaths.
B) He says that God knows them but they are uncountable and unceasing.
C) He says that the people of Paradise and Hell do perish.
D) He says that God's knowledge is not applicable to breaths.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi shows that God knows all things, including the unending breaths of Paradise and Hell, and that created beings remain only by God's preservation, not by their own nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself assuming that your own existence is a given, something you deserve? How does the fact that you remain only by God's preservation (ibqā') change your sense of entitlement?
?
If you truly believed that God knows every single moment of your existence—every breath—and that those breaths are uncountable and unceasing only by His will, would you live this day differently? What would you change right now?
?
The Jahmiyya feared that affirming God's knowledge of endless breaths would lead to equality between God and creation. Do you ever subtly compare yourself to God, perhaps by feeling independent or self-sufficient? How can you cultivate the awareness that you are radically contingent?
